# Routing Table — Distance Vector with Withdrawals

Related documentation:

- [mesh.md](mesh.md) — network layer overview
- [roadmap.md](roadmap.md) — full iteration plan
- [protocol.md](protocol.md) — wire protocol

Source: `internal/core/domain/peer.go`, `internal/core/routing/types.go`, `internal/core/routing/table.go`, `internal/core/routing/announce.go`, `internal/core/routing/announce_builder.go`, `internal/core/routing/announce_state.go`, `internal/core/node/table_router.go`, `internal/core/node/routing_announce.go`, `internal/core/node/routing_relay.go`, `internal/core/node/routing_resolver.go`, `internal/core/node/routing_session.go`, `internal/core/node/routing_hop_ack.go`, `internal/core/node/routing_drain.go`, `internal/core/node/routing_provider.go`, `internal/core/rpc/routing_commands.go`

### Overview

The routing package implements a distance-vector routing table for the CORSA mesh network. It replaces blind gossip delivery with directed forwarding based on hop-count metrics. Gossip remains the fallback when no route is known.

### Type safety: PeerIdentity and PeerAddress

`domain.PeerIdentity` (Ed25519 fingerprint, 40-char lowercase hex) and `domain.PeerAddress` (transport host:port) are defined types based on `string` (`internal/core/domain/peer.go`). They enforce compile-time distinction between routing identities and transport addresses, preventing the class of bugs where one is passed where the other is expected. The routing package re-exports both as type aliases (`routing.PeerIdentity = domain.PeerIdentity`) so callers need only import `routing`. All `RouteEntry` fields (`Identity`, `Origin`, `NextHop`), `AnnounceEntry` fields, `Snapshot` map keys, and `Table` function signatures use `PeerIdentity`. Transport-level maps (`sessions`, `health`, `pending`) and peer lifecycle functions use `PeerAddress`. Wire protocol `Frame` fields remain `string`; casts happen at the boundary between wire format and internal typed code.

**Безопасность типов: PeerIdentity и PeerAddress.** `domain.PeerIdentity` (отпечаток Ed25519, 40 символов hex) и `domain.PeerAddress` (транспортный host:port) — определённые типы на основе `string` (`internal/core/domain/peer.go`). Они обеспечивают различие на этапе компиляции между идентификаторами маршрутизации и транспортными адресами, предотвращая класс ошибок, когда один передаётся вместо другого. Пакет routing реэкспортирует оба как алиасы типов. Все поля `RouteEntry`, `AnnounceEntry`, ключи `Snapshot` и сигнатуры функций `Table` используют `PeerIdentity`. Транспортные карты (`sessions`, `health`, `pending`) и функции жизненного цикла используют `PeerAddress`. Поля протокола `Frame` остаются `string`; приведение происходит на границе между wire-форматом и внутренним типизированным кодом.

### Core types

`RouteEntry` is the **boundary value** carried across the public Table API (`UpdateRoute` argument, `Lookup` return, wire ingest projection). Pre-Phase-1 the entry shape doubled as the in-storage dedup key under the triple `(Identity, Origin, NextHop)`. Post-Phase-1 storage moved to per-`(Identity, Uplink)` `UplinkClaim` (see "Storage model" subsection below); `RouteEntry` retains the legacy field set on the boundary so existing callers and the wire projection stay unchanged, but the **dedup key on storage is now `(Identity, Uplink)` only** — the `Origin` field on a `RouteEntry` returned from `Lookup` is a synthesised marker (`localOrigin` or, fallback, the destination `Identity` itself), not the original wire-frame Origin. The original wire-frame Origin is preserved internally as `UplinkClaim.LastIngressOrigin` / `SeenOriginSeqs` for mixed-version interop admission rules and never re-emitted as-is on the wire.

`AnnounceEntry` is the wire-safe projection of `RouteEntry`. It contains only the four fields transmitted in `announce_routes` frames (Identity, Origin, Hops, SeqNo). Produced by `RouteEntry.ToAnnounceEntry()` or `Table.AnnounceTo()`. The wire carries the sender's local hop count as-is — the receiver adds +1 when inserting into its own table (receive path).

`Table` is the thread-safe local storage for routes. It owns this node's identity (`localOrigin`) and a monotonic SeqNo counter per destination (`seqCounters`). Public operations: `AddDirectPeer`, `RemoveDirectPeer`, `UpdateRoute`, `WithdrawRoute`, `RefreshDirectPeers`, `TickTTL`, `Announceable`, `AnnounceTo`, `Lookup`, and `Snapshot`.

`Snapshot` is an immutable point-in-time copy of the full table, safe to read without locks.

`AddDirectPeerResult` describes the outcome of a peer connect: the `RouteEntry` created or refreshed, and a `Penalized` flag indicating whether flap detection applied a shortened TTL.

`RemoveDirectPeerResult` describes the outcome of a peer disconnect: wire-ready `[]AnnounceEntry` withdrawals (SeqNo already incremented, Hops=16) for own-origin direct routes, plus a count of transit routes silently invalidated locally, plus `ExposedBackups []PeerIdentity` — identities where invalidation revealed a surviving non-withdrawn backup route (used by `onPeerSessionClosed` to trigger drain).

`RouteUpdateStatus` is the three-valued outcome of `UpdateRoute`: `RouteAccepted` (new or improved route inserted), `RouteUnchanged` (existing alive route reconfirmed — same SeqNo, same or worse trust/hops, not expired), `RouteRejected` (tombstone block, stale SeqNo, or expired unchanged). Callers use this to distinguish new routing events from benign reconfirmations: `handleAnnounceRoutes` drains pending on both `RouteAccepted` and `RouteUnchanged`, and logs three separate counters (accepted, unchanged, rejected) instead of the previous two (accepted, rejected).

`RouteUpdateStatus` — трёхзначный результат `UpdateRoute`: `RouteAccepted` (новый или улучшенный маршрут вставлен), `RouteUnchanged` (существующий живой маршрут подтверждён — тот же SeqNo, те же или худшие trust/hops, не истёкший), `RouteRejected` (блокировка tombstone, устаревший SeqNo, или истёкший unchanged). Вызывающий код использует это для разделения новых routing-событий и штатных подтверждений: `handleAnnounceRoutes` дрейнит pending и при `RouteAccepted`, и при `RouteUnchanged`, и логирует три отдельных счётчика (accepted, unchanged, rejected) вместо прежних двух (accepted, rejected).

`AnnounceSnapshot` is a canonical, aggregated, peer-specific view of route entries ready for wire transmission. The wire-shape contract has two distinct layers — see `internal/core/routing/announce_builder.go`'s AnnounceSnapshot doc-comment for the full split. The production layer (`routeStore.AnnounceProjectionFor`) enforces per-Identity live-winner collapse AND live-vs-tombstone exclusivity: at most ONE live winner per Identity, with own-direct tombstones suppressed when a live alternative exists (see "Live-vs-tombstone exclusivity on the wire" in Key invariants below). When no live winner exists for an Identity, the tombstone IS emitted so receivers evict promptly. The structural layer (`BuildAnnounceSnapshot` itself) does NOT re-enforce exclusivity — synthetic test fixtures bypassing AnnounceProjectionFor may feed both a live entry and a tombstone for the same Identity, and ComputeDelta keys on `(Identity, IsWithdrawn)` so both slots can coexist for synthetic input. Entries are sorted deterministically by `(Identity, Hops, Origin)` — Identity ascending, live winner (Hops ≤ 15) before any tombstone (Hops = 16) within an Identity group, Origin lex tie-break. A nil `*AnnounceSnapshot` represents "no snapshot sent yet" (empty state) and is semantically different from a snapshot with zero entries.

**Per-Identity aggregation (Phase 0.x hot-fix, 2026-05; Phase 1 storage swap finalised, 2026-Q3).** Field-data analysis of a 100-node mesh routes.json snapshot showed 12.7× wire amplification: 6072 stored RouteEntry rows, 1440 `(Identity, Origin)` buckets, but only 113 reachable identities. The hot-fix added per-Identity live-winner collapse (after the legacy per-`(Identity, Origin)` aggregation stage that has since been removed): picks min `Hops`, then higher `SeqNo`, then deterministic `Extra` byte order, then deterministic `Origin` lexicographic tie-break. Phase 1 then completed the receive-side half: storage migrated to per-`(Identity, Uplink)` `UplinkClaim` shape (Origin dropped from the dedup key — see "Storage model" subsection below for the full contract), so the on-table redundancy also collapsed from 7.6× back to baseline. **Live-vs-tombstone wire exclusivity:** when a live winner exists for an Identity, own-direct tombstones for that Identity are SUPPRESSED on the wire (the live emit already overrides any prior receiver state, and emitting a trailing tombstone via the outbound SeqNo synthesiser would assign it a strictly greater SeqNo than the live winner and flip the receiver to withdrawn). Tombstones DO emit when no live alternative exists — the receiver still needs the dead signal so they evict instead of waiting on TTL. Outbound wire volume per cycle drops ~12.7× in the typical case (no tombstones); on disconnect events one extra entry per affected Identity rides along WHEN no live backup exists. Backward compat: legacy peers continue to receive `(Identity, Origin, Hops, SeqNo)` frames with `Origin = localOrigin` (sender-originated semantic — matches their per-`(Identity, Origin, NextHop)` triple shape on storage); our contribution to their storage drops from N entries per `(Identity, Origin)` lineage to (1 live winner OR 1 tombstone) per Identity, and the SeqNo timeline they observe is the synthesised per-`(Identity, sender)` shape from the outbound SeqNo helpers.

`AnnouncePeerState` holds per-peer announce send state: the last successfully sent snapshot, timestamps for full sync attempts/successes and delta sends, a `needsFullResync` flag, and disconnect tracking for eviction. All mutable fields are accessed exclusively through thread-safe methods (`View()`, `RecordFullSyncAttempt()`, `RecordFullSyncSuccess()`, `RecordDeltaSendSuccess()`). Direct field access from outside the package is forbidden. Owned by `AnnounceStateRegistry`.

`AnnounceStateRegistry` manages per-peer `AnnouncePeerState` instances. Thread-safe for concurrent access from the announce loop and session lifecycle callbacks. Provides `GetOrCreate`, `MarkDisconnected`, `MarkReconnected`, `EvictStale`, `MarkInvalid`, and `Cleanup`. Disconnected state is evicted after `2 * flapWindow`. The clock source is injectable for tests.

`AnnounceSnapshot` — каноническое, агрегированное, peer-specific представление записей маршрутов, готовое к передаче. Wire-shape контракт имеет два слоя — см. AnnounceSnapshot doc-comment в `internal/core/routing/announce_builder.go` для полного split'а. Production слой (`routeStore.AnnounceProjectionFor`) enforce'ит per-Identity live-winner collapse И live-vs-tombstone exclusivity: максимум ОДИН live winner per Identity, с own-direct tombstones suppress'енными когда live альтернатива есть (см. "Live-vs-tombstone exclusivity на проводе" в Ключевых инвариантах ниже). Когда live winner для Identity отсутствует — tombstone эмитится, чтобы receivers evict'ились promptly. Структурный слой (`BuildAnnounceSnapshot` сам) НЕ re-enforce'ит exclusivity — синтетические test fixtures, обходящие AnnounceProjectionFor, могут передать и live entry и tombstone для одной Identity, а ComputeDelta keys на `(Identity, IsWithdrawn)`, поэтому оба слота могут coexist для synthetic input. Записи отсортированы детерминированно по `(Identity, Hops, Origin)` — Identity ASC, live winner (Hops ≤ 15) перед tombstone (Hops = 16) внутри Identity-группы, Origin lex tie-break. Nil `*AnnounceSnapshot` означает «ни один snapshot ещё не отправлен» и семантически отличается от snapshot с нулём записей.

**Per-Identity агрегация (Phase 0.x hot-fix, 2026-05; Phase 1 storage swap финализирован, 2026-Q3).** Field-data анализ 100-нодной mesh routes.json snapshot'и показал 12.7× wire amplification: 6072 stored RouteEntry строк, 1440 `(Identity, Origin)` bucket'ов, но только 113 reachable identity'ев. Hot-fix добавил per-Identity live-winner collapse (после legacy per-`(Identity, Origin)` aggregation stage, который с тех пор удалён): выбирает min `Hops`, затем higher `SeqNo`, затем deterministic `Extra` byte order, затем deterministic `Origin` lexicographic tie-break. Phase 1 затем завершил receive-side половину: storage мигрирован на per-`(Identity, Uplink)` `UplinkClaim` shape (Origin dropped из dedup key — см. "Модель хранения" подсекцию ниже для полного контракта), поэтому on-table redundancy тоже схлопнулся с 7.6× к baseline. **Live-vs-tombstone wire exclusivity:** при наличии live winner для Identity, own-direct tombstones для этой Identity SUPPRESS'ятся на проводе (live emit уже override'ит любое prior receiver state, а emit'нувшийся trailing tombstone через outbound SeqNo synthesiser получил бы строго более высокий SeqNo чем live winner и flip'нул бы receiver в withdrawn). Tombstones DO эмитятся когда live альтернативы нет — receiver всё ещё нуждается в dead signal чтобы evict вместо ожидания TTL. Outbound wire volume per cycle падает в ~12.7× в typical case (без tombstones); на disconnect events одна дополнительная запись per affected Identity ride'ится рядом КОГДА no live backup exists. Backward compat: legacy peer'ы продолжают получать `(Identity, Origin, Hops, SeqNo)` кадры с `Origin = localOrigin` (sender-originated semantic — соответствует их per-`(Identity, Origin, NextHop)` triple shape на storage); наш вклад в их storage drops с N записей per `(Identity, Origin)` lineage до (1 live winner OR 1 tombstone) per Identity, и SeqNo timeline который они наблюдают — синтезированный per-`(Identity, sender)` shape из outbound SeqNo helpers.

`AnnouncePeerState` — per-peer состояние отправки анонсов: последний успешно отправленный snapshot, timestamps попыток/успехов full sync и delta send, флаг `needsFullResync`, отслеживание disconnect для eviction. Все мутабельные поля доступны только через потокобезопасные методы (`View()`, `RecordFullSyncAttempt()`, `RecordFullSyncSuccess()`, `RecordDeltaSendSuccess()`). Владелец — `AnnounceStateRegistry`.

`AnnounceStateRegistry` — реестр per-peer `AnnouncePeerState`. Потокобезопасный для одновременного доступа из цикла анонсов и колбэков жизненного цикла сессий. Предоставляет `GetOrCreate`, `MarkDisconnected`, `MarkReconnected`, `EvictStale`, `MarkInvalid` и `Cleanup`. Disconnected-состояние удаляется через `2 * flapWindow`. Источник времени внедряется для тестов.

### Storage model

Internal storage lives in `routing.routeStore` (`internal/core/routing/route_store.go`) and is **per-`(Identity, Uplink)` `UplinkClaim`**, where `Uplink` is the direct-peer identity that announced the claim to us:

```go
type UplinkClaim struct {
    Uplink            PeerIdentity              // direct peer who told us this claim
    Hops              uint8                     // their announced hops + 1
    SeqNo             uint64                    // upstream wire SeqNo
    Source            RouteSource               // direct / hop_ack / announcement
    UpdatedAt         time.Time
    ExpiresAt         time.Time                 // zero for direct
    Withdrawn         bool
    Extra             json.RawMessage           // forward-compat wire metadata
    LastIngressOrigin PeerIdentity              // sticky wire-frame Origin (mixed-version)
    SeenOriginSeqs    map[PeerIdentity]uint64   // per-Origin high-water (lazy)
    AttestedSig       []byte                    // reserved для Phase 4 (mesh_attested_links_v1)
}
```

`LastIngressOrigin` и `SeenOriginSeqs` поддерживают mixed-version interop admission rules — см. "Mixed-version interop" под Key invariants ниже для full contract. Storage держит за-Identity bucket с до `MaxNextHopsPerOrigin` LIVE claims (knob name kept ради operator stability; semantic post-A1 — K live UplinkClaims per Identity). Withdrawn claims (tombstones) живут вне K-counted slots и bypass cap entirely — SeqNo-resurrection guard не evict'ится под cap pressure.

The boundary `RouteEntry` is synthesised on demand by `toRouteEntry` (in `uplink_claim.go`): it takes a stored `UplinkClaim` plus the destination `Identity` plus the table's `localOrigin` and produces a wire-shaped value with `Origin = localOrigin` (or fallback to `Identity` when `localOrigin` is empty). This synthesis is what lets the public Table API stay source-compatible with pre-Phase-1 callers while storage internals migrated.

### Key invariants

**Per-Identity SeqNo monotonicity.** Sequence numbers are managed at two scopes:

- *Own-origin advance counter*: `seqCounters[Identity]` is the monotonic counter for routes this node originates (direct peers). It advances automatically in `AddDirectPeer` / `RemoveDirectPeer` / `InvalidateAllVia` and is synced forward by `UpdateRoute` ONLY when the accepted entry has `Source == RouteSourceDirect` AND `Origin == localOrigin` (see "SeqNo counter consistency" below — the Source gate prevents synthesised `Origin == localOrigin` on hop_ack-promotion paths from poisoning the counter with foreign SeqNo values).
- *Per-`(Identity, sender)` wire timeline*: every outbound wire emit (live winner, own-direct tombstone passthrough, broadcast withdrawal) gets its SeqNo synthesised through `routeStore.nextOutboundSeqLockedPerPeer` / `nextOutboundSeqLockedBroadcast`. The helpers maintain a per-`(Identity, content-sig)` cache plus three watermarks (`outboundMax`, `outboundBroadcastMax[Identity]`, `outboundPeerMax[(Identity, peer)]`) so the receiver observes a strictly monotonic SeqNo on each `(Identity, sender)` pair regardless of which uplink's `claim.SeqNo` contributed the content. The watermarks defend against two A→B→A flavours — broadcast-driven (own-direct fanout crossing a per-peer cache) and per-peer winner-switch (alternate-uplink preference shift advancing a single peer past the cached value). Both are pinned by `TestAnnounceTo_*` regression suites in `announce_builder_test.go`.

**Dedup key.** The pair `(Identity, Uplink)` uniquely identifies a stored `UplinkClaim`. Different uplinks for the same destination Identity produce independent claims (multipath). The legacy boundary RouteEntry shape carries an `Origin` field, but post-Phase-1 it is NOT part of the dedup key — only `(Identity, NextHop=Uplink)` is consulted by `routeStore.findByUplinkLocked`.

**Live-vs-tombstone exclusivity on the wire.** When a live winner exists for an Identity, own-direct tombstones for the same Identity are SUPPRESSED on the wire by `AnnounceProjectionFor` (storage retains the tombstone for the local SeqNo-resurrection guard). Emitting both would let `nextOutboundSeqLockedPerPeer` assign the tombstone a strictly greater SeqNo than the live winner (peerMax advances on the live emit), and the receiver's monotonic-SeqNo timeline would converge on the tombstone — dropping the Identity even though we just offered a backup uplink. Tombstones DO emit when no live alternative exists.

**Mixed-version interop admission rules.** Pre-A1 transits use per-Origin SeqNo counters and shift their per-Identity winner between Origin lineages per cycle. Post-A1 storage applies five admission rules in fixed order inside `ApplyUpdate` to keep the legacy stream interop intact:

1. Pre-check guard rejects cross-Origin updates whose incoming Origin has a recorded `SeenOriginSeqs` high-water at or above `entry.SeqNo` (stale-replay on the Origin's own timeline).
2. HopAck override preserves the stored `LastIngressOrigin` / `SeenOriginSeqs` when the entry came from `confirmRouteViaHopAck` (synthetic `Origin == localOrigin` from `Lookup`, not a wire observation).
3. Cross-Origin live-vs-tombstone at equal SeqNo promotes the live entry through the same cap-aware `AdmitNew` detach+readmit used in the SeqNo > old branch.
4. Standard SeqNo branches (>, ==, <) — the stale-SeqNo branch additionally admits a cross-Origin update when it strictly improves on hops, trust, or replaces a tombstone (cross-Origin lineage shift).
5. Reconfirmation TTL refresh gate is hops-only (`incoming.Hops == old.Hops`), NOT source-equality — so a wire re-announce after a HopAck promotion still refreshes TTL.

All five rules are dormant for A1-to-A1 traffic (post-A1 senders emit `Origin = localOrigin` constant across cycles, so cross-Origin gates never fire).

**Split horizon.** When building an announcement for peer A, claims where `Uplink == A` are omitted. No fake `hops=16` withdrawal is sent — that would violate the receiver's SeqNo monotonicity invariant.

**Withdrawal semantics.** A withdrawal sets `Hops = 16` (infinity) and requires strictly `SeqNo > old.SeqNo`. On the wire, only the origin may send a withdrawal. On peer disconnect, `RemoveDirectPeer` withdraws own-origin direct routes (returned as wire-ready `[]AnnounceEntry` with SeqNo already incremented) and silently invalidates transit routes locally. Transit nodes do not emit wire withdrawals for routes they did not originate. Own-origin tombstones remain in the table for `defaultTTL` (120s) and are included in `AnnounceTo` output **only when no live alternative exists for the same Identity** — when a live winner is present, the live-vs-tombstone exclusivity rule (round 5l, see "Per-Identity aggregation" above) SUPPRESSES the tombstone emit to avoid the ordering hazard where `nextOutboundSeqLockedPerPeer` would assign the trailing tombstone a strictly greater SeqNo than the live winner and flip the receiver to withdrawn. The announce-delta retry path therefore covers tombstone redelivery only in the no-live-alternative case; whenever a live alternate exists, the live entry's emit already supersedes any prior receiver-side state. Transit tombstones are excluded from `AnnounceTo` regardless — only the origin may emit wire withdrawals.

**Семантика отзыва.** Отзыв устанавливает `Hops = 16` (бесконечность) и требует строго `SeqNo > old.SeqNo`. На проводе только origin может отправить withdrawal. При отключении peer'а `RemoveDirectPeer` отзывает own-origin direct routes (возвращаемые как wire-ready `[]AnnounceEntry` с уже инкрементированным SeqNo) и молча инвалидирует transit routes локально. Transit-узлы не отправляют wire withdrawals для маршрутов, которые они не порождали. Own-origin tombstones остаются в таблице на `defaultTTL` (120s) и включаются в вывод `AnnounceTo` **только когда для той же Identity нет live alternative** — при наличии live winner правило live-vs-tombstone exclusivity (round 5l, см. "Per-Identity агрегация" выше) SUPPRESS'ит tombstone-emit, чтобы избежать ordering hazard'а: `nextOutboundSeqLockedPerPeer` присвоил бы trailing tombstone строго более высокий SeqNo, чем live winner, и flip'нул бы receiver в withdrawn. Поэтому announce-delta retry для tombstones срабатывает только в no-live-alternative случае; пока live alternate существует, его emit уже override'ит любое prior receiver-side состояние. Transit tombstones исключаются из `AnnounceTo` независимо — только origin имеет право отправлять wire withdrawals.

**Announce frame is not a destructive snapshot.** A single `announce_routes` frame is **not** a complete authoritative snapshot of the sender's entire routing table. The absence of a route entry in a particular `announce_routes` frame does **not** imply withdrawal and does **not** mean implicit deletion. A receiver must not remove previously learned routes solely because they are missing from the latest announce frame. Withdrawal is expressed exclusively through an explicit route entry with `hops >= HopsInfinity`, which only the origin has the right to send. This invariant is critical for the correctness of partial (delta) announcements: a sender may legitimately send only changed entries in an `announce_routes` frame, and the receiver must continue to use previously learned routes that were not included in the update.

**Announce-кадр не является деструктивным снимком.** Один кадр `announce_routes` **не является** полным авторитетным снимком всей таблицы маршрутизации отправителя. Отсутствие записи маршрута в конкретном кадре `announce_routes` **не означает** withdrawal и **не означает** неявного удаления. Получатель не должен удалять ранее изученные маршруты только потому, что они отсутствуют в последнем announce-кадре. Withdrawal выражается исключительно через явную запись маршрута с `hops >= HopsInfinity`, которую имеет право отправлять только origin. Этот инвариант критически важен для корректности частичных (delta) анонсов: отправитель может законно отправить только изменившиеся записи в кадре `announce_routes`, а получатель должен продолжать использовать ранее изученные маршруты, не включённые в обновление.

**First-sync wire-frame invariant.** The first full-sync that follows routing-capable session establishment MUST leave the sender as a self-contained baseline frame — either the legacy `announce_routes` wire frame via `PeerSender.SendAnnounceRoutes` (for v1/v2 peers), or the compact `route_announce_v3` frame with `kind="full"` via `PeerSender.SendRouteAnnounceV3` (for peers that advertise the v3 triplet `mesh_routing_v1` + `mesh_routing_v3` + `mesh_relay_v1`). A v3 `kind="full"` frame is self-contained by design — it carries the sender's complete view of the peer's routes plus the table epoch needed for the receiver's epoch-watermark gate (see `docs/protocol/route_announce_v3.md` "Epoch handling") — so it qualifies as a valid baseline on the same footing as the legacy frame. The v2 `routes_update` frame (`PeerSender.SendRoutesUpdate`) and the v3 `kind="delta"` frame are BOTH permitted ONLY for later incremental cycles of a peer that has already received its first matching baseline successfully AND has the corresponding upgrade capability negotiated. Rationale: a delta frame (v2 or v3) carries an incremental update computed against a baseline the peer already has; a fresh session has no baseline, so a delta would arrive unanchored and the receiver either drops it or enters a split-world state vs the sender. Mixed-version networks MUST never observe `routes_update` nor `route_announce_v3 kind="delta"` on a fresh session on the wire — only `announce_routes` or `route_announce_v3 kind="full"`.

Code call sites implementing the invariant:

- `sendConnectTimeFullSync` in `internal/core/node/routing_announce.go` — shared core for inbound (`sendFullTableSyncToInbound`) and outbound (`sendOutboundFullTableSync`) connect-time full-table sync. Picks `Service.SendRouteAnnounceV3` with `kind="full"` when the peer advertises the v3 triplet (v1 + v3 + relay); otherwise falls back to `Service.SendAnnounceRoutes`. NEVER `SendRoutesUpdate` and NEVER `kind="delta"` — both are deltas and would arrive against no baseline. Short-circuits on an empty snapshot by recording a baseline without sending any wire frame (empty-baseline, see "Announce frame is not a destructive snapshot" above and the `empty-baseline` branch of the convergence flow below).
- `sendFullAnnounce` in `internal/core/routing/announce.go` — forced-full / periodic-forced-full path in `AnnounceLoop`. Wire-send is delegated to one of two single-call-site helpers: `sendV3Full` (the only in-package call site for `PeerSender.SendRouteAnnounceV3` with `kind="full"`, fired when the peer negotiated the v3 triplet) or `sendLegacyFull` (the only in-package call site for `PeerSender.SendAnnounceRoutes` for full sync, fired for v1/v2 peers). Any future branch picking `SendRoutesUpdate` or `kind="delta"` here MUST NOT be introduced — the helper names, their doc-comments, and the guard tests below are independent review tripwires.

Runtime protection is anchored by guard tests: `TestAnnounceLoop_ForcedFull_UsesLegacySender_NonEmptySnapshot` (`internal/core/routing/announce_invariant_test.go`) fails the test immediately if `SendRoutesUpdate` is ever called on the forced-full path; `TestConnectTimeFullSync_UsesLegacySender_NonEmptySnapshot` and `TestConnectTimeFullSync_EmptySnapshot_NoWireFrame` (`internal/core/node/routing_integration_connect_sync_test.go`) observe the actual wire frame via `net.Pipe` and assert legacy vs v2 explicitly. A regression that swaps the first-sync wire frame surfaces there before reaching CI on a real peer.

Empty-baseline note: when the peer-specific snapshot is empty after split-horizon filtering, both call sites record a full-sync baseline without sending any wire frame. This empty-baseline behaviour is orthogonal to the first-sync wire-frame invariant (which is about which frame to use when one IS sent) — guard tests for the invariant deliberately seed at least one route so the wire-level assertion has something to compare against; empty-baseline is its own contract and has a dedicated regression test.

Empty-baseline + delta receive-gate interaction. Empty-baseline records `RecordFullSyncSuccess` locally but emits no wire frame, so the peer never observes any baseline arrival in the new session and the peer-side gate (`AnnouncePeerState.hasReceivedBaseline` on the receiver) stays false. To keep the symmetric receive gate honest, every `AnnouncePeerState` carries TWO per-peer wire-baseline-sent flags, one per upgraded delta generation: `wireBaselineSentToPeer` mirrors the v2 receive gate (set by `MarkWireBaselineSent` after a successful `SendAnnounceRoutes` in `sendConnectTimeFullSync`, `sendLegacyFull`, `sendIncrementalAnnounce`, or `fanoutAnnounceRoutes`), and `wireBaselineV3SentToPeer` mirrors the v3 receive gate (set by `MarkWireBaselineV3Sent` after a successful `route_announce_v3 kind="full"` in `sendConnectTimeFullSync` or `sendV3Full`). While the matching flag is false, `AnnounceLoop.announceToAllPeers` overrides the corresponding delta classification (`deltaModeV2` or `deltaModeV3`) down to legacy `deltaModeV1` — the very first observable wire frame in a session is therefore always a self-contained baseline (legacy `announce_routes` if no upgraded baseline has shipped, or the corresponding `kind="full"` if it has). Both flags reset on every session boundary (`MarkDisconnected` / `MarkReconnected`). Without the override, an empty connect-time baseline followed by a non-empty cycle would emit a delta against a peer whose receive gate is still closed; the peer drops the frame and emits `request_resync`, costing one wasted round-trip per session for every empty-then-non-empty progression. The downgrades are observable in the cycle log lines as `announce_v2_downgraded_no_wire_baseline` and `announce_v3_downgraded_no_wire_baseline` respectively.

**Инвариант первого sync-кадра.** Первый full-sync после установления routing-capable session ОБЯЗАН уходить от отправителя как self-contained baseline-кадр — либо legacy wire-frame `announce_routes` через `PeerSender.SendAnnounceRoutes` (для v1/v2 peer'ов), либо компактный `route_announce_v3` с `kind="full"` через `PeerSender.SendRouteAnnounceV3` (для peer'ов, рекламирующих v3-triplet `mesh_routing_v1` + `mesh_routing_v3` + `mesh_relay_v1`). v3-кадр `kind="full"` self-contained by design — он несёт полный view маршрутов peer'а плюс table epoch, необходимый для epoch-watermark gate получателя (см. `docs/protocol/route_announce_v3.md` "Epoch handling"), — поэтому он квалифицируется как valid baseline наравне с legacy-кадром. V2-кадр `routes_update` (`PeerSender.SendRoutesUpdate`) и v3 `kind="delta"` ОБА допустимы ТОЛЬКО для последующих incremental-циклов peer'а, который уже успешно получил соответствующий baseline И с которым согласован соответствующий upgrade-capability. Причина: delta-кадр (v2 или v3) несёт incremental-обновление, рассчитанное относительно baseline, которого у fresh session ещё нет; в отсутствие baseline delta приходит «в воздух», получатель либо отбрасывает его, либо входит в расщеплённое состояние с отправителем. Mixed-version сеть в принципе не должна видеть на fresh session ни `routes_update`, ни `route_announce_v3 kind="delta"` — только `announce_routes` или `route_announce_v3 kind="full"`.

Code call-sites, реализующие инвариант:

- `sendConnectTimeFullSync` в `internal/core/node/routing_announce.go` — общий core для inbound (`sendFullTableSyncToInbound`) и outbound (`sendOutboundFullTableSync`) connect-time full-table sync. Выбирает `Service.SendRouteAnnounceV3` с `kind="full"`, когда peer advertise'ит v3-triplet (v1 + v3 + relay); иначе fallback на `Service.SendAnnounceRoutes`. НИКОГДА `SendRoutesUpdate` И НИКОГДА `kind="delta"` — оба delta-кадры и пришли бы к peer'у без baseline. Замыкает ветку пустого snapshot-а на запись baseline без отправки wire-кадра (семантика empty-baseline описана в разделе «Announce-кадр не является деструктивным снимком» выше и в ветке `empty-baseline` диаграммы convergence ниже).
- `sendFullAnnounce` в `internal/core/routing/announce.go` — forced-full / periodic-forced-full путь в `AnnounceLoop`. Отправка wire-кадра делегируется одному из двух single-call-site helper'ов: `sendV3Full` (единственная в пакете точка вызова `PeerSender.SendRouteAnnounceV3` с `kind="full"`, срабатывает когда peer negotiated v3-triplet) или `sendLegacyFull` (единственная в пакете точка вызова `PeerSender.SendAnnounceRoutes` для full sync, срабатывает для v1/v2 peer'ов). Любая будущая ветка, выбирающая `SendRoutesUpdate` или `kind="delta"`, не должна появляться здесь — имена helper'ов, их doc-комментарии и guard-тесты ниже — независимые review-тревоги.

Runtime-защита опирается на guard-тесты: `TestAnnounceLoop_ForcedFull_UsesLegacySender_NonEmptySnapshot` (`internal/core/routing/announce_invariant_test.go`) валит тест сразу, если на forced-full пути когда-либо вызывается `SendRoutesUpdate`; `TestConnectTimeFullSync_UsesLegacySender_NonEmptySnapshot` и `TestConnectTimeFullSync_EmptySnapshot_NoWireFrame` (`internal/core/node/routing_integration_connect_sync_test.go`) наблюдают реальный wire-кадр через `net.Pipe` и явно проверяют legacy vs v2. Регрессия, подменяющая wire-кадр первого sync-а, всплывает здесь раньше, чем доезжает до CI на живом peer-е.

Про empty-baseline: когда peer-specific snapshot после split-horizon пустой, оба call-site записывают full-sync baseline без отправки wire-кадра. Это поведение ортогонально first-sync-инварианту (он — о том, какой кадр использовать, если кадр всё-таки отправляется) — guard-тесты для инварианта сознательно сажают в таблицу хотя бы один маршрут, чтобы wire-level assertion было с чем сравнивать; empty-baseline — отдельный контракт с собственным regression-тестом.

Взаимодействие empty-baseline и delta receive-gate. Empty-baseline пишет `RecordFullSyncSuccess` локально, но не отправляет ни одного wire-кадра, так что peer в новой сессии не видит ни одного baseline-кадра и peer-side гейт (`AnnouncePeerState.hasReceivedBaseline` на receiver'е) остаётся false. Чтобы симметричный receive-gate работал честно, в каждом `AnnouncePeerState` хранится ДВА per-peer wire-baseline-sent флага, по одному на upgraded delta-generation: `wireBaselineSentToPeer` — зеркало v2-receive-gate (ставит `MarkWireBaselineSent` после успешного `SendAnnounceRoutes` в `sendConnectTimeFullSync`, `sendLegacyFull`, `sendIncrementalAnnounce` и `fanoutAnnounceRoutes`), а `wireBaselineV3SentToPeer` — зеркало v3-receive-gate (ставит `MarkWireBaselineV3Sent` после успешного `route_announce_v3 kind="full"` в `sendConnectTimeFullSync` или `sendV3Full`). Пока соответствующий флаг false, `AnnounceLoop.announceToAllPeers` принудительно понижает соответствующую delta-классификацию (`deltaModeV2` или `deltaModeV3`) до legacy `deltaModeV1` — первый наблюдаемый wire-кадр в сессии всегда self-contained baseline (legacy `announce_routes`, если upgraded baseline ещё не отгружен, либо соответствующий `kind="full"`, если отгружен). Оба флага сбрасываются на каждой границе сессии (`MarkDisconnected` / `MarkReconnected`). Без override-а пустой connect-time baseline с последующим непустым циклом отправил бы delta peer-у с закрытым receive-gate; peer дропнет кадр и пришлёт `request_resync`, стоимость — один лишний round-trip на сессию для каждой комбинации «пусто → не пусто». Downgrade'ы видны в cycle-лог-строках как `announce_v2_downgraded_no_wire_baseline` и `announce_v3_downgraded_no_wire_baseline` соответственно.

**Self-route (local identity).** When `localOrigin` is configured, `Lookup()` and `Snapshot()` synthesize a local route entry for the node's own identity (`Hops=0`, `Source=RouteSourceLocal`). This route is not stored in the table — it is injected on read. It never expires, is never withdrawn, and is never included in announcements (`AnnounceTo`/`Announceable`). Peers discover this node via their own direct routes. The self-route ensures that a node can always resolve itself in the routing table without requiring an external peer session. `Snapshot().TotalEntries` and `Snapshot().ActiveEntries` do not count the synthetic self-route — these counters describe persisted table state and stay consistent with `ActiveSize()`. `reachableFromSnapshot`, `reachableIDsFrame`, and `fetch_route_summary` exclude `RouteSourceLocal` entries because reachability is about remote peers, not the node itself. `UpdateRoute` rejects `RouteSourceLocal` with `ErrLocalSourceReserved` — this source is purely synthetic and must never be persisted.

```mermaid
flowchart LR
    A["Lookup(localOrigin)"] --> B["Synthesize RouteEntry\nHops=0, Source=Local\nExpiresAt=zero"]
    B --> C["Return in results\n(prepended, highest trust)"]
    D["Snapshot()"] --> B
    E["AnnounceTo() / Announceable()"] -.->|"excluded"| F["Never sent on wire"]
    G["UpdateRoute(Source=Local)"] -.->|"rejected"| H["ErrLocalSourceReserved"]
```
*Diagram — Self-route: synthetic, read-only, never stored or announced*

**Собственный маршрут (локальная идентичность).** Когда `localOrigin` настроен, `Lookup()` и `Snapshot()` синтезируют локальный маршрут для собственной идентичности ноды (`Hops=0`, `Source=RouteSourceLocal`). Этот маршрут не хранится в таблице — он инжектируется при чтении. Он никогда не истекает, никогда не отзывается и никогда не включается в анонсы (`AnnounceTo`/`Announceable`). Пиры обнаруживают эту ноду через свои собственные прямые маршруты. Собственный маршрут гарантирует, что нода всегда может разрешить саму себя в таблице маршрутизации без внешней пир-сессии. `Snapshot().TotalEntries` и `Snapshot().ActiveEntries` не считают синтетический self-route — эти счётчики описывают персистированное состояние таблицы и согласованы с `ActiveSize()`. `reachableFromSnapshot`, `reachableIDsFrame` и `fetch_route_summary` исключают записи `RouteSourceLocal`, поскольку достижимость касается удалённых пиров, а не самой ноды. `UpdateRoute` отклоняет `RouteSourceLocal` с `ErrLocalSourceReserved` — этот источник чисто синтетический и не должен персистироваться.

```mermaid
flowchart LR
    A["Lookup(localOrigin)"] --> B["Синтез RouteEntry\nHops=0, Source=Local\nExpiresAt=zero"]
    B --> C["Возврат в результатах\n(prepended, высший trust)"]
    D["Snapshot()"] --> B
    E["AnnounceTo() / Announceable()"] -.->|"исключён"| F["Никогда не отправляется на провод"]
    G["UpdateRoute(Source=Local)"] -.->|"отклонён"| H["ErrLocalSourceReserved"]
```
*Диаграмма — Self-route: синтетический, read-only, никогда не хранится и не анонсируется*

**Trust hierarchy.** Per triple, `local > direct > hop_ack > announcement`. The `local` source (TrustRank=3) is reserved for the synthetic self-route and is never stored in the table. At the same SeqNo, a higher-trust source replaces a lower-trust one. Confirming one triple via hop_ack does not affect other triples, even those sharing the same NextHop.

**Иерархия доверия.** На тройку: `local > direct > hop_ack > announcement`. Источник `local` (TrustRank=3) зарезервирован для синтетического собственного маршрута и никогда не хранится в таблице. При одинаковом SeqNo источник с более высоким доверием заменяет источник с более низким.

**Route selection order.** `Lookup()` ranks routes by the Phase 2 `CompositeScore` (base hop-count term + source-trust bonus + RTT bonus + health penalty — see "Route health and composite scoring" below and `docs/protocol/route_health.md` for the formula). Source trust still nudges the ranking via the bonus (local/direct +20, hop_ack +10, announcement 0), so for equal hops/health/RTT a higher-trust source wins; but unlike the pre-Phase-2 sort, source trust no longer dominates hop count unconditionally — a Good 1-hop announcement can outscore a Bad 3-hop direct. `HealthDead` claims are filtered before ranking, with one exemption: `RouteSourceDirect` (own-origin) claims stay selectable even when Dead and are scored with a `Bad`-equivalent penalty, because Direct lifecycle is session-driven rather than health-driven.

**TTL expiry.** Learned routes (from announcements and hop_ack) carry an `ExpiresAt` timestamp (default 120s from insertion). `TickTTL()` removes expired entries and returns a slice of identities where the expiry exposed a surviving non-withdrawn backup route — `routingTableTTLLoop` uses this to trigger `drainPendingForIdentities` for immediate delivery via the backup. Learned routes are refreshed naturally when the neighbor re-announces them. When a same-SeqNo re-announcement arrives for an expired entry, `UpdateRoute` accepts it as a valid refresh — the origin has not changed the route, it is simply re-confirming it. When a same-SeqNo same-source same-hops re-announcement arrives for an *alive* learned entry — an exact reconfirmation — `UpdateRoute` returns `RouteUnchanged` and extends `ExpiresAt` to `now + defaultTTL`. The wire-level reconfirmation renews the lifetime even though no field a delta consumer cares about has changed. Without this refresh, no-op suppression on the send side would let learned routes age out between forced full syncs (see "Refresh interval invariant" below). A *weaker* incoming entry — same SeqNo but worse hops or lower trust — also returns `RouteUnchanged` but must NOT extend ExpiresAt: the old entry is the better path and the receiver wants to keep it, but allowing the optimistic earlier hops=N entry to be refreshed by a hops=N+1 reapplication would freeze it indefinitely and block natural TTL-driven reconvergence onto the actually-current path when the origin does not bump SeqNo. Direct routes are also exempt from this refresh: their `ExpiresAt` is zero by design (see "Direct route lifecycle" below) and overwriting it would convert a never-expiring entry into a 120s-ageing one — `IsExpired` returns false for zero, so an alive direct route would otherwise reach this branch alongside learned ones.

**Direct route lifecycle.** Own-origin direct routes use `ExpiresAt=zero` (never expire by time). Their lifetime is managed entirely by the session lifecycle: `AddDirectPeer` creates them on socket connect, `RemoveDirectPeer` withdraws them on socket close. This is event-driven — no periodic TTL refresh is needed. `RemoveDirectPeer` sets `Hops=HopsInfinity` and `ExpiresAt=now+defaultTTL` on the withdrawn entry, creating a tombstone that `TickTTL` cleans up after the default TTL window. This design eliminates a class of race conditions where `TickTTL` could permanently delete an active direct route between `RefreshDirectPeers` cycles, making a connected peer invisible to the routing table. `UpdateRoute` enforces the zero-`ExpiresAt` invariant at primary normalization: any `RouteSourceDirect` entry that arrives there — through a state restore, a defensive re-application, or the explicit Direct-via-`UpdateRoute` test paths — has its `ExpiresAt` forced to zero before insertion regardless of what the caller supplied, so no caller can accidentally land an active direct entry with a finite TTL that `TickTTL` would later evict.

```mermaid
stateDiagram-v2
    [*] --> Active: Socket connect → AddDirectPeer
    Active --> Active: Announce loop reads route (ExpiresAt=zero, never expires)
    Active --> Withdrawn: Socket close → RemoveDirectPeer (Hops=16, ExpiresAt=now+120s)
    Withdrawn --> [*]: TickTTL removes tombstone after TTL
    Withdrawn --> Active: Reconnect → AddDirectPeer (new SeqNo)
```
*Diagram — Direct route lifecycle: event-driven, no TTL expiry*

**Refresh interval invariant.** Learned routes on neighbors carry a `defaultTTL` lifetime (120s). The send side suppresses wire emission when the per-peer delta is empty (see `announce_cycle_complete` log line: `announce_skipped_noop`), so the only mechanism that renews TTL on an unchanged lineage is the periodic forced full sync, which fires every `EffectiveForcedFullSyncInterval(AnnounceInterval)`. The bound is:

```
EffectiveForcedFullSyncInterval(AnnounceInterval) <= DefaultTTL / 2
```

`EffectiveForcedFullSyncInterval(AnnounceInterval) = min(ForcedFullSyncMultiplier × AnnounceInterval, DefaultTTL/2)` — the cap is enforced inside the helper itself, so any operator-configured `AnnounceInterval` (via `CORSA_ANNOUNCE_INTERVAL_SECONDS`) yields a forced-full-sync cadence ≤ TTL/2. At the default values (`multiplier=2`, `interval=30s`, `TTL=120s`) the inequality is tight: forced full sync fires every 60s = TTL/2 = exactly when half the TTL has elapsed, so a single dropped or late-arriving sync still leaves the next attempt before the lifetime ends. For shorter operator-configured intervals (e.g. 10s → forced cadence 20s) the cadence is below TTL/2 by a wider margin; for `AnnounceInterval ≥ TTL/2` the cap clamps to TTL/2.

The Run loop tick period is chosen by `chooseTickInterval(AnnounceInterval, EffectiveForcedFullSyncInterval(AnnounceInterval))` so the tick is a divisor of the cap — forced-full deadlines therefore land exactly on a tick rather than "deadline + up to one tick" later. Without that, an operator setting `AnnounceInterval=45s` would tick at 45s, observe the 60s deadline only at the 90s wake, and stretch the actual cadence past TTL/2. See the helper's doc-comment in `internal/core/routing/announce.go` for the gcd-based algorithm and the busy-loop floor that protects against non-second-aligned inputs.

Forced-full retry rate-limit window is clamped to `min(MinForcedFullSyncInterval, EffectiveForcedFullSyncInterval(AnnounceInterval))` so it never exceeds the projected cadence — without the clamp, an operator setting a short interval (e.g. 10s, forced cadence 20s) would have the second forced attempt blocked by the fixed 30s rate-limit window and the actual cadence would silently stretch to 30s, contradicting the helper's projection. Default 30s interval is unaffected (clamp is a no-op when `forcedFullSyncInterval ≥ 30s`).

The invariant is enforced by two pieces of machinery, both of which must hold for the contract to be intact:

- send-side cadence — guarded by a small bench of unit tests in `internal/core/routing/announce_test.go` and `internal/core/routing/announce_invariant_test.go`:
    - `TestRoutingConstants_RefreshIntervalInvariant` — pins the default-constants compile-time inequality `ForcedFullSyncMultiplier × DefaultAnnounceInterval ≤ DefaultTTL/2` so a change to any of the three constants without rechecking is caught.
    - `TestEffectiveForcedFullSyncInterval_CappedAtTTLHalf` — pins the cap inside the helper itself for ANY operator-configured AnnounceInterval (`min(2 × interval, DefaultTTL/2)`), so an operator setting a value above TTL/2 cannot push the cadence past the freshness boundary.
    - `TestAnnounceLoop_TickInterval_DividesBothCadences` — pins that `chooseTickInterval` returns a tick that divides both the operator interval AND the forced cap, so forced-full deadlines land EXACTLY on a tick rather than "deadline + up to one tick" later.
    - `TestAnnounceLoop_TickInterval_BusyLoopGuard` — pins the 1-second floor on production cadences so non-second-aligned operator inputs (e.g. `59s + 1ns`) cannot collapse `gcd` to a sub-second value and turn `time.NewTicker` into a busy loop.
    - `TestAnnounceLoop_ForcedFullRateLimit_ClampedToForcedFullCap` — pins the round 15.6 clamp `min(MinForcedFullSyncInterval, EffectiveForcedFullSyncInterval(AnnounceInterval))` so the rate-limit window cannot stretch the actual forced-full cadence past the helper's projection.
    - `TestAnnounceLoop_TriggerDoesNotDelayForcedFullDeadline` — pins the round 15.9 P1 fix: the `triggerCh` handler in `AnnounceLoop.Run` MUST NOT call `ticker.Reset(tickInterval)`. With triggers arriving slightly faster than the natural tick (e.g. connect/disconnect storms during a churn event), each Reset would push the next periodic wake forward, the forced-full deadline check would only catch a deadline at the next trigger past the cap, and the actual forced-full gap would silently exceed `EffectiveForcedFullSyncInterval(AnnounceInterval)`. The test drives `AnnounceInterval=200ms` (cap=400ms) with triggers every 180ms and asserts the wire-send gap stays within `cap + 50ms` jitter tolerance — the bug shape produces ~540ms gaps and fails cleanly.
- receive-side TTL extension — `UpdateRoute`'s `RouteUnchanged` branch (`internal/core/routing/table.go`) refreshes `ExpiresAt` on alive learned entries only when the incoming entry is an exact reconfirmation (same source AND same hops), leaves weaker re-applications (worse hops, lower trust) without a TTL bump so reconvergence still works, and leaves direct-route entries with their `ExpiresAt=zero` untouched. The same file's primary normalization step forces `ExpiresAt=zero` for every `RouteSourceDirect` insert/replace so a direct entry can never reach the table with a finite TTL through any UpdateRoute path. Guarded by `TestUpdateRouteRefreshesTTLOnUnchangedLiveRoute`, `TestUpdateRouteUnchangedWorseHopsDoesNotRefreshTTL`, `TestUpdateRouteDirectInsertPreservesZeroExpiry`, `TestUpdateRouteUnchangedDirectRoutePreservesZeroExpiry` (all in `internal/core/routing/table_test.go`), and the end-to-end `TestAnnounceLoop_ForcedFullSync_RefreshesLearnedRouteBeforeExpiry` (`internal/core/routing/announce_ttl_refresh_test.go`).

Removing any of the send-side guards or the receive-side TTL extension regresses the "best route flaps" symptom: learned `hops=N` routes through a hub disappear for up to `DefaultTTL - EffectiveForcedFullSyncInterval(AnnounceInterval)` per cycle (at the default 30s interval that's 60s; for shorter operator-configured intervals it shrinks proportionally), the local `Lookup` rotates onto longer transit paths, and the visible best-route field oscillates between optimal and degraded values until the next full sync repopulates the optimal lineage.

**Operator tuning — announce interval and overload gate.** Two config knobs let densely-connected receivers shed CPU without violating the freshness invariant:

- `CORSA_ANNOUNCE_INTERVAL_SECONDS` (`config.Node.AnnounceInterval`). Overrides the periodic delta-cycle period. Default unset → `routing.DefaultAnnounceInterval` (30s). Operators of densely-connected nodes (>10 direct peers) may raise to 45-60s to halve the per-peer delta-computation CPU. The forced-full-sync cadence is independently capped at `DefaultTTL/2` by `routing.EffectiveForcedFullSyncInterval` regardless of the configured interval, so the freshness invariant above ALWAYS holds. Setting `AnnounceInterval = DefaultTTL/2` collapses every tick into a forced full sync (no in-between deltas), which is appropriate when the sender is CPU-bound by delta computation across many peers; the trade-off is that state propagation latency loses the mid-cycle delta granularity.
- `CORSA_OVERLOAD_GOROUTINE_THRESHOLD` (`config.Node.OverloadGoroutineThreshold`). When set to a positive integer, the announce loop consults a goroutine-count proxy (`runtime.NumGoroutine()`) at the start of each cycle. If goroutines exceed the threshold, delta sends to peers that don't owe a forced full sync this round are suppressed; forced-full-sync still fires on its TTL/2 schedule so receivers never see stale routes. Disabled by default (zero threshold). A reasonable starting value for hub nodes is observed `NumGoroutine` under normal load × 2-3 — typically 5000-10000 for a densely-connected node. The cumulative engaged-cycle counter is surfaced through `fetchRouteSummary` under the `overload.engaged_cycles` field (see `docs/rpc/routing.md`) so operators can see whether backpressure is firing in production without attaching a debugger. Goroutine count is a proxy because each inbound frame spawns at least one goroutine; sustained backlog produces visible pile-up. The proxy may be replaced with explicit per-peer inbox length aggregation in a future iteration.

**NextHop is peer identity.** Routing operates at identity level, not transport addresses. A single peer identity may have multiple concurrent TCP sessions; session selection happens later in `node.Service` via the identity-to-session(s) index that resolves identities to active connections.

**Entry validation.** `RouteEntry.Validate()` enforces structural invariants at insert time: Identity, Origin, and NextHop must be non-empty; Hops must be in range [1, 16] for stored routes. Source-specific rules: direct routes (`RouteSourceDirect`) must have `Hops=1` and `NextHop == Identity` (directly connected neighbor); local routes (`RouteSourceLocal`) must have `Hops=0`. Malformed entries are rejected by `UpdateRoute` before acquiring locks or touching table state. `UpdateRoute` additionally rejects `RouteSourceLocal` entries with `ErrLocalSourceReserved` — this source is purely synthetic and must never be persisted, preventing any caller from injecting a zero-hop highest-trust route for an arbitrary identity. `UpdateRoute` also enforces an origin guard for direct routes: when `localOrigin` is configured, a `RouteSourceDirect` entry whose `Origin != localOrigin` is rejected with `ErrDirectForeignOrigin`. This prevents callers from injecting impossible direct routes for foreign origins that would outrank all announcement/hop_ack routes in `Lookup` and never be eligible for own-origin withdrawal handling on disconnect.

**Валидация записей.** `RouteEntry.Validate()` проверяет структурные инварианты при вставке: Identity, Origin и NextHop не должны быть пустыми; Hops в диапазоне [1, 16] для хранимых маршрутов. Правила по источникам: direct-маршруты (`RouteSourceDirect`) должны иметь `Hops=1` и `NextHop == Identity`; локальные (`RouteSourceLocal`) — `Hops=0`. `UpdateRoute` дополнительно отклоняет `RouteSourceLocal` записи с ошибкой `ErrLocalSourceReserved` — этот источник чисто синтетический и не должен персистироваться. `UpdateRoute` также проверяет origin guard для direct-маршрутов: `RouteSourceDirect` с `Origin != localOrigin` отклоняется с `ErrDirectForeignOrigin`.

**Wire projection boundary.** The boundary between table-model and wire-format is explicit: `AnnounceTo(excludeVia)` returns `[]AnnounceEntry` with split horizon applied. The wire carries the sender's local hop count — no +1 is applied on the sender side; the receiver adds +1 when inserting into its own table . `RemoveDirectPeer` returns wire-ready `[]AnnounceEntry` withdrawals with SeqNo already incremented. Callers building `announce_routes` frames use `AnnounceTo` or `RemoveDirectPeer` results directly — no manual arithmetic is needed.

**SeqNo counter consistency.** When `UpdateRoute` accepts an own-direct entry (`Source == RouteSourceDirect` AND `Origin == localOrigin`), it synchronizes the monotonic counter: `seqCounters[identity] = max(counter, entry.SeqNo)`. This ensures that tables pre-populated via `UpdateRoute` (e.g., restored from a snapshot or received via full sync) do not cause subsequent `AddDirectPeer`/`RemoveDirectPeer` to emit a stale SeqNo. The `Source == RouteSourceDirect` gate is critical post-Phase-1: the `toRouteEntry` synthesiser sets `Origin = localOrigin` on EVERY claim returned from `Lookup` (regardless of underlying claim source), so hop_ack-promotion paths (where `confirmRouteViaHopAck` reads via `Lookup` and resubmits with `Source = RouteSourceHopAck`) carry foreign SeqNo values under a `localOrigin` Origin. Without the Source gate those foreign SeqNos would poison our own-direct counter and the next own-direct withdrawal would emit a stale SeqNo that legacy receivers reject.

### Integration

```mermaid
flowchart LR
    subgraph Before["Before (gossip)"]
        A1[Node A] -->|flood| B1[Node B]
        A1 -->|flood| C1[Node C]
        B1 -->|flood| D1[Node D]
        C1 -->|flood| D1
    end

    subgraph After["After (table routing)"]
        A2[Node A] -->|relay via table| B2[Node B]
        B2 -->|relay via table| D2[Node D]
        A2 -.->|gossip fallback| C2[Node C]
    end
```
*Diagram — Message delivery: gossip flood vs table-directed relay*

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant A as Node A
    participant B as Node B
    participant F as Target F

    Note over A: Lookup(F) → RouteEntry{F, via B, hops=2}
    A->>B: relay_message(to=F, msg_id=99)
    B->>F: relay_message(to=F, msg_id=99)
    F->>B: relay_hop_ack(msg_id=99)
    B->>A: relay_hop_ack(msg_id=99)
    Note over A: Route (F, origin=F, via B) → source="hop_ack"
```
*Diagram — Table-directed relay with hop_ack confirmation*

**Convergence.** The announce loop (`routing/announce.go`) runs periodic announcements at the operator-configured cadence (`AnnounceInterval`, default 30 seconds, override via `CORSA_ANNOUNCE_INTERVAL_SECONDS`) and supports triggered updates on connect/disconnect events. The loop uses per-peer announce state (`routing/announce_state.go`) to track what was last sent to each peer. On each cycle, raw route entries from `Table.AnnounceTo(peer)` are aggregated into a canonical peer-specific snapshot. Post-Phase-1 the heavy lifting happens in `routeStore.AnnounceProjectionFor` upstream of the snapshot builder: it does the per-Identity live-winner collapse inline (min Hops → higher SeqNo → verified-sig tie-break (Round-26: `AttestedSigVerified=true` beats unsigned, mirrors `scoreSignedBonus` in `Lookup`/`AnnounceTargetFor`) → Extra tie-break → Uplink lex), enforces live-vs-tombstone exclusivity (live winner emitted alone; tombstone emitted only when no live alternative exists), and synthesises the outbound wire SeqNo through `nextOutboundSeqLockedPerPeer` / `nextOutboundSeqLockedBroadcast` (see Key invariants → "Per-Identity SeqNo monotonicity"). `BuildAnnounceSnapshot` then runs as a thin defensive pass on the projection output: exact-duplicate removal, per-`(Identity, Origin, SeqNo, Withdrawn)` collapse (defends against synthetic test-fixture inputs that bypass AnnounceProjectionFor), and per-Identity tombstone collapse so that synthetic multi-tombstone snapshots produce stable deltas. The legacy pre-A1 per-`(Identity, Origin)` max-SeqNo stage was removed in Phase 1 — `Origin = localOrigin` is constant across all post-A1 emits, so the stage had become destructive (would collapse the live winner and an own-direct tombstone for the same Identity into a single slot by SeqNo race). The result is sorted by `(Identity, Hops, Origin)` — Identity ascending, live winner before any tombstone within an Identity group, Origin lex tie-break. If the snapshot is unchanged from the last send, no frame is emitted (no-op suppression). If only a subset changed, only the delta entries are sent in an `announce_routes` frame. A forced full sync is performed on new peer connect and periodically every `EffectiveForcedFullSyncInterval(AnnounceInterval)` (= `min(ForcedFullSyncMultiplier × AnnounceInterval, DefaultTTL/2)` — at default 30s interval that is 60s; for shorter operator intervals it is `2 × AnnounceInterval`; for longer ones it clamps at TTL/2 = 60s). The cadence is bound by the **Refresh interval invariant** below: forced cadence ≤ DefaultTTL/2. Without that bound, learned routes on neighbors silently expire between cycles because no-op suppression skips wire emission for unchanged snapshots. If the peer-specific snapshot is empty at full-sync time (e.g. split horizon filtered all routes when announcing back to a single-route peer), the full-sync baseline is recorded as successful without sending a wire frame — the peer learns nothing new, and subsequent cycles use the delta path normally (empty-baseline). Forced full sync attempts are rate-limited by `min(MinForcedFullSyncInterval, EffectiveForcedFullSyncInterval(AnnounceInterval))` to prevent flooding when a peer is repeatedly marked `NeedsFullResync` — the clamp ensures the rate-limit window never stretches the actual cadence past the projected one (e.g. for `AnnounceInterval=10s`, rate-limit clamps from the fixed 30s constant down to 20s = forced cadence). The rate limit is bypassed for peers that have never successfully received any data (`LastSentSnapshot == nil`) — a failed first attempt must not block retry. Incoming `announce_routes` frames are processed by `handleAnnounceRoutes` in `node/routing_announce.go` — each route gets +1 hop on the receiver side. Withdrawals (hops=16) are applied via `Table.WithdrawRoute`, but only from the origin sender (`Origin == senderIdentity`). When `WithdrawRoute` receives a withdrawal for an unseen `(Identity, Uplink=NextHop)` pair, it creates a tombstone entry (hops=HopsInfinity) with the withdrawal's SeqNo. This prevents a delayed older announcement from resurrecting a withdrawn lineage — the tombstone's SeqNo blocks any stale update for the same `(Identity, Uplink)` pair. The withdrawal frame's `Origin` is preserved on the public `WithdrawRoute` API for backward compat with pre-A1 callers but is stored only as `LastIngressOrigin` lineage metadata on the tombstone (post-Phase-A storage keys per-`(Identity, Uplink)` — see "Storage model" above; the legacy three-tuple triple is gone from the dedup key). Tombstones expire via normal TTL. **Tombstones are independent of `MaxNextHopsPerOrigin`:** they are appended unconditionally and excluded from the cap counter, so a saturated bucket of K live routes still admits new tombstones (the cap protects only the K live slots). This is a deliberate design trade-off — see "RIB compaction" — that keeps the SeqNo resurrection guard intact under cap pressure. The `mesh_routing_v1` capability is now advertised during handshake. The announce loop covers both outbound sessions and inbound-only connections. Target discovery via `routingCapablePeers()` requires both `mesh_routing_v1` and `mesh_relay_v1` — a routing-only peer (no relay) is excluded because routes through it would create non-deliverable paths.

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    A["Event: connect / disconnect / withdrawal / periodic tick"] --> B["Build peer-specific canonical snapshot\n(Table.AnnounceTo → BuildAnnounceSnapshot)"]
    B --> C["Compare with per-peer cache"]
    C --> D{"New peer\nor forced full?"}
    D -- "Yes" --> E0{"Snapshot empty?"}
    E0 -- "Yes" --> E1["Record empty baseline\n(no wire frame)"]
    E0 -- "No" --> E["Send full announce_routes"]
    D -- "No" --> F{"Diff vs last send?"}
    F -- "No" --> G["No-op: skip send"]
    F -- "Yes" --> H["Send announce_routes\nwith changed entries only"]
    E1 --> I["Update per-peer cache"]
    E --> I
    H --> I
```
*Diagram — Announce loop: per-peer send decision / Диаграмма — Цикл анонсов: решение об отправке per-peer*

**Extra invariant in aggregation.** `Extra` (opaque `json.RawMessage`) MUST be identical for all table entries sharing the same `(Identity, Origin, SeqNo)` lineage. The origin node sets `Extra` once per SeqNo; every relay forwards it unchanged. If `BuildAnnounceSnapshot` detects differing `Extra` values for the same lineage during Stage 2 aggregation, it logs a warning (`announce_aggregation_extra_mismatch`) and falls back to deterministic tie-break (larger canonical `Extra` wins). Such divergence indicates relay data corruption or protocol version mismatch and requires investigation.

**Инвариант Extra при агрегации.** `Extra` (опаковый `json.RawMessage`) ДОЛЖЕН быть идентичным для всех записей таблицы с одинаковым lineage `(Identity, Origin, SeqNo)`. Origin-нода устанавливает `Extra` один раз для каждого SeqNo; каждый relay пересылает его без изменений. Если `BuildAnnounceSnapshot` обнаруживает расхождение `Extra` для одного lineage при агрегации Stage 2, логируется предупреждение (`announce_aggregation_extra_mismatch`) и применяется детерминированный tie-break (побеждает больший канонический `Extra`). Такое расхождение указывает на повреждение данных relay или несовместимость версий протокола и требует расследования.

**Конвергенция.** Цикл анонсов (`routing/announce.go`) выполняет периодические анонсы с operator-configured cadence (`AnnounceInterval`, по умолчанию 30 секунд, override через `CORSA_ANNOUNCE_INTERVAL_SECONDS`) и поддерживает triggered-обновления при подключении/отключении. Цикл использует per-peer состояние анонсов (`routing/announce_state.go`) для отслеживания того, что было отправлено каждому peer'у. На каждом цикле raw-записи маршрутов из `Table.AnnounceTo(peer)` агрегируются в канонический peer-specific snapshot. Post-Phase-1 тяжёлая работа происходит upstream — в `routeStore.AnnounceProjectionFor`: он делает per-Identity live-winner collapse inline (min Hops → higher SeqNo → verified-sig tie-break (Round-26: `AttestedSigVerified=true` побеждает unsigned, mirror'ит `scoreSignedBonus` в `Lookup`/`AnnounceTargetFor`) → Extra tie-break → Uplink lex), enforce'ит live-vs-tombstone exclusivity (live winner эмитится один; tombstone эмитится только когда live alternative нет) и синтезирует outbound wire SeqNo через `nextOutboundSeqLockedPerPeer` / `nextOutboundSeqLockedBroadcast` (см. Ключевые инварианты → "Per-Identity SeqNo monotonicity"). `BuildAnnounceSnapshot` (`routing/announce_builder.go`) затем работает как тонкий defensive pass над projection output: exact-duplicate removal, per-`(Identity, Origin, SeqNo, Withdrawn)` collapse (защита от synthetic test-fixture inputs, обходящих AnnounceProjectionFor) и per-Identity tombstone collapse, чтобы synthetic multi-tombstone snapshots давали стабильные delta. Legacy pre-A1 per-`(Identity, Origin)` max-SeqNo stage была удалена в Phase 1 — `Origin = localOrigin` константа на всех post-A1 emit'ах, поэтому stage стала destructive (collapse'нула бы live winner и own-direct tombstone одной Identity в один slot по SeqNo race). Результат сортируется по `(Identity, Hops, Origin)` — Identity ASC, live winner перед любым tombstone внутри Identity-группы, Origin lex tie-break. Если snapshot не изменился по сравнению с последней отправкой, кадр не отправляется (no-op suppression). Если изменилась только часть, отправляются только delta-записи в кадре `announce_routes`. Принудительная полная синхронизация выполняется при подключении нового peer'а и периодически каждые `EffectiveForcedFullSyncInterval(AnnounceInterval)` (= `min(ForcedFullSyncMultiplier × AnnounceInterval, DefaultTTL/2)` — при default 30s interval это 60s; для коротких operator-интервалов это `2 × AnnounceInterval`; для длинных clamp'ится до TTL/2 = 60s). Каденс ограничен **инвариантом интервала refresh** ниже: forced cadence ≤ DefaultTTL/2. Без этого ограничения learned-маршруты у соседей тихо истекают между циклами — no-op suppression пропускает отправку для unchanged snapshot. Если peer-specific snapshot пуст на момент full sync (например, split horizon отфильтровал все маршруты при анонсе обратно single-route peer'у), baseline записывается как успешный без отправки wire-кадра — peer не узнаёт ничего нового, а последующие циклы используют delta path как обычно (empty-baseline). Попытки forced full sync ограничены `min(MinForcedFullSyncInterval, EffectiveForcedFullSyncInterval(AnnounceInterval))` для предотвращения flood при повторном `NeedsFullResync` — clamp гарантирует, что rate-limit window никогда не растягивает actual cadence за projected (например, для `AnnounceInterval=10s` rate-limit clamp'ится с fixed 30s константы до 20s = forced cadence). Rate limit обходится для peer'ов, которые никогда успешно не получали данных (`LastSentSnapshot == nil`) — неудачная первая попытка не должна блокировать retry.

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    A["Событие: connect / disconnect / withdrawal / periodic tick"] --> B["Построить peer-specific канонический snapshot\n(Table.AnnounceTo → BuildAnnounceSnapshot)"]
    B --> C["Сравнить с per-peer cache"]
    C --> D{"Новый peer\nили forced full?"}
    D -- "Да" --> E0{"Snapshot пуст?"}
    E0 -- "Да" --> E1["Записать empty baseline\n(без wire frame)"]
    E0 -- "Нет" --> E["Отправить full announce_routes"]
    D -- "Нет" --> F{"Есть diff\nпо сравнению с прошлой отправкой?"}
    F -- "Нет" --> G["No-op: пропустить отправку"]
    F -- "Да" --> H["Отправить announce_routes\nтолько с изменившимися entries"]
    E1 --> I["Обновить per-peer cache"]
    E --> I
    H --> I
```
*Диаграмма — Цикл анонсов: решение об отправке per-peer*

**Receive-path validation.** `handleAnnounceRoutes` enforces three safety invariants before accepting any wire announcement: (1) **Sender identity validation** — the sender identity must be a valid 40-char lowercase hex fingerprint (`identity.IsValidAddress`). For inbound connections, the identity is read from `connPeerHello.identity` (the hello frame's `Address` field), not from `connPeerHello.address` (the listen address used for health tracking). This distinction is critical for NATed peers that advertise a non-routable listen address (e.g. `127.0.0.1:64646`) — using the listen address as routing identity would cause all announcements from such peers to be rejected as malformed. For outbound sessions, the identity is read from `session.peerIdentity` (set from the welcome frame). (2) **Own-origin rejection** — announcements where `Origin == localIdentity` from a foreign sender are silently dropped. Only this node may originate routes under its own identity; accepting a forged own-origin entry would let a neighbor poison the monotonic SeqNo counter via `syncSeqCounterLocked`. (3) **Transit withdrawal rejection** — wire withdrawals (`hops >= 16`) where `Origin != senderIdentity` are silently dropped. Only the origin may emit a wire withdrawal; transit nodes must invalidate locally and stop advertising. All three guards are enforced before `UpdateRoute`/`WithdrawRoute` to prevent malformed data from reaching the table.

**Direct-route capability gate.** `onPeerSessionEstablished(peerIdentity, caps)` takes the peer's full negotiated capability set and flattens it internally to a `hasRelayCap := sessionHasCap(caps, domain.CapMeshRelayV1)` local decision that controls whether `AddDirectPeer` is called. A direct route in the distance-vector table advertises that this node can relay DMs to the destination. If the peer cannot accept `relay_message` frames (legacy or gossip-only node), the route would be non-deliverable — other routing-capable nodes would learn a path that silently fails at the last hop. The outbound call site passes the session's `capabilities` slice directly. The inbound call site resolves the per-connection capability snapshot via `connCapabilitiesForID(id)`. Peers without `mesh_relay_v1` still connect and exchange gossip normally but are never advertised as direct destinations in the routing table. The full capability list is also forwarded to `AnnounceStateRegistry.MarkReconnected` so the announce plane can make mode decisions without a second `peerMu` round-trip — the registry takes a defensive copy internally, so callers may pass session-owned slices unchanged.

**Multi-session identity with dual counters.** `node.Service` maintains two per-identity counters: `identitySessions` (total active sessions) and `identityRelaySessions` (relay-capable sessions only). `AddDirectPeer()` is called on the `identityRelaySessions` 0→1 transition (first relay-capable session). `RemoveDirectPeer()` is called on the `identityRelaySessions` 1→0 transition (last relay-capable session closes). This means a non-relay first session does not block a later relay session from creating the direct route, and closing the last relay session withdraws the route even if legacy sessions remain. `onPeerSessionClosed(peerIdentity, caps)` receives the same capability set that was passed to the matching `onPeerSessionEstablished` call so both counters stay balanced on every transition. Total session count cleanup happens independently.

**Persistent caps as a derived view of the chosen target.** `AnnouncePeerState.capabilities` is the persistent capability snapshot consulted by `classifyDeltaMode` at delta-mode selection. It is reconciled to the per-cycle `AnnounceTarget.Capabilities` at the very start of each per-peer goroutine in `AnnounceLoop.announceToAllPeers` via `AnnounceStateRegistry.UpdateCapabilities`. This is the single source of truth: the persistent snapshot is a derived view of the same session `routingCapablePeers` actually picked this cycle. No lifecycle-hook variant updates persistent caps on session establishment or close — `MarkReconnected` writes the initial snapshot for a fresh peer but additional routing-capable sessions, relay-only sessions, and non-relay sessions all leave the snapshot unchanged at the lifecycle-hook level. Why no hook variant works: `routingCapablePeers` dedupes overlapping sessions for one identity by map iteration order, so two cycles can pick different sessions when overlapping routing-capable sessions for the same peer have different negotiated caps; a partial close (the session that previously refreshed the snapshot disappears while an older routing-capable session remains) leaves the persistent caps describing a session that is no longer the target; a relay-only session (no `mesh_routing_v1`) is counted in `identityRelaySessions` but cannot be picked by `routingCapablePeers` as a target, so its caps must not poison the persistent snapshot — the older routing-capable session would still be selected and `classifyDeltaMode` would read mismatched sources. Cycle-time reconciliation sidesteps every one of these races: the cycle reads the same caps twice (once via target, once via persistent snapshot just synced from target), so `classifyDeltaMode` always sees agreeing inputs in production. The divergence path in `classifyDeltaMode` remains as a defensive net but is unreachable from the loop while the cycle-time sync stands; if a future call site introduces a second writer to `AnnouncePeerState.capabilities` or routes around the cycle sync, `MarkInvalid` + legacy delta on the current cycle is the safe fallback. `UpdateCapabilities` is intentionally narrow: it touches only the capability slice and never resets `hasReceivedBaseline`, `wireBaselineSentToPeer`, or `needsFullResync` — caps are an identity-level property reflected from active sessions; they must not influence baseline-gate state, which tracks wire-history with the peer identity in the current session window.

**Persistent caps как производная вьюха выбранного target-а.** `AnnouncePeerState.capabilities` — persistent capability-снимок, который читает `classifyDeltaMode` при выборе delta-mode. Он реконсилируется с per-cycle `AnnounceTarget.Capabilities` в самом начале каждой per-peer goroutine в `AnnounceLoop.announceToAllPeers` через `AnnounceStateRegistry.UpdateCapabilities`. Это единственный источник истины: persistent-снимок — derived-view той же сессии, которую `routingCapablePeers` фактически выбрал в этом цикле. Никакой lifecycle-hook не обновляет persistent caps на установке/закрытии сессии — `MarkReconnected` пишет первоначальный снимок для нового peer-а, но дополнительные routing-capable сессии, relay-only сессии и не-relay сессии все оставляют снимок неизменным на уровне lifecycle-hook-ов. Почему ни один hook-вариант не работает: `routingCapablePeers` дедуплицирует overlapping-сессии одной identity по порядку итерации мапы, поэтому два цикла могут выбрать разные сессии, когда overlapping routing-capable сессии того же peer-а имеют разные согласованные caps; partial close (сессия, которая раньше обновила снимок, исчезает, а другая routing-capable остаётся) оставляет persistent caps описывающими сессию, которая больше не target; relay-only сессия (без `mesh_routing_v1`) учитывается в `identityRelaySessions`, но `routingCapablePeers` её не выбирает как target, поэтому её caps не должны отравлять persistent-снимок — иначе старая routing-capable сессия всё равно будет выбрана target-ом и `classifyDeltaMode` прочитает рассогласованные источники. Cycle-time реконсиляция обходит все эти гонки: цикл читает одни и те же caps дважды (один раз через target, второй — через persistent-снимок, только что синхронизированный из target-а), поэтому `classifyDeltaMode` в продакшене всегда видит согласованные входы. Divergence-путь в `classifyDeltaMode` остаётся как defensive net, но недостижим из цикла пока стоит cycle-time sync; если будущий call site введёт второго писателя в `AnnouncePeerState.capabilities` или обойдёт cycle sync, `MarkInvalid` + legacy delta в текущем цикле — безопасный fallback. `UpdateCapabilities` намеренно узкий: трогает только capability-slice и никогда не сбрасывает `hasReceivedBaseline`, `wireBaselineSentToPeer` или `needsFullResync` — caps это identity-level свойство, отражённое из активных сессий; они не должны влиять на baseline-gate-стейт, который трекает wire-историю с peer-identity в текущем session-окне.

**Full-table sync on connect.** Both outbound and inbound connection paths send an immediate full-table sync (`routingTable.AnnounceTo(peerIdentity)`) to the newly connected peer. This ensures symmetric initial convergence regardless of connection direction. The sync is gated on both `mesh_routing_v1` and `mesh_relay_v1` capabilities — matching the steady-state announce loop contract. A routing-only peer (mesh_routing_v1 without mesh_relay_v1) would learn routes it cannot deliver on the data plane, so it is excluded from connect-time sync as well. The outbound path checks `sessionHasCapability(address, capMeshRoutingV1) && sessionHasCapability(address, capMeshRelayV1)` in `establishPeerSession`. The inbound path checks `connHasCapability(conn, capMeshRoutingV1) && connHasCapability(conn, capMeshRelayV1)` in `trackInboundConnect`. Both paths pass the peer's Ed25519 identity fingerprint (`peerIdentity`) to `AnnounceTo` — not the transport or listen address. This is critical for NATed inbound peers whose listen address (e.g. `127.0.0.1:64646`) differs from their identity fingerprint; passing the transport address would break split horizon filtering. Legacy peers without either capability are silently skipped. Split horizon is applied — routes learned from the connecting peer are excluded. If the resulting peer-specific snapshot is empty (e.g. the only route is the peer's own direct route, excluded by split horizon), the full-sync baseline is recorded without sending a wire frame (empty-baseline); subsequent announce cycles use the delta path normally. If the send fails (session queue full, connection lost between handshake and sync), a warning is logged (`routing_outbound_full_sync_failed` or `routing_inbound_full_sync_failed`). The peer will still receive the table on the next periodic announce cycle.

**Flap dampening.** The routing table tracks per-peer disconnect frequency to prevent link flaps from churning routes and flooding the network with announcements. Each `RemoveDirectPeer` call records a withdrawal timestamp. When a peer accumulates `flapThreshold` (default 3) disconnects within `flapWindow` (default 120s), it enters hold-down state for `holdDownDuration` (default 30s). During hold-down, `AddDirectPeer` still creates the route (connectivity is preserved), but the `AddDirectPeerResult.Penalized` flag signals to the caller that the triggered announce should be suppressed — the route will be picked up by the next periodic announce cycle, reducing announcement churn. Direct routes themselves have no TTL (see Direct route lifecycle above), so flap dampening affects only the announce timing, not route expiry. `TickTTL` cleans up stale flap state once both hold-down and the flap window have expired. All thresholds are configurable via `WithFlapWindow`, `WithFlapThreshold`, `WithHoldDownDuration`, and `WithPenalizedTTL` options.

```mermaid
stateDiagram-v2
    [*] --> Normal
```
