- A `RouteEntry` with `Source=hop_ack` for a `NextHop` not yet in the bucket — when constructed by a caller that has authentic `Origin` and `SeqNo` metadata — displaces the worst announcement under the trust-tier rule (announcement < hop_ack), so promotions land regardless of whether the bucket is saturated with weaker tier entries. **Caveat:** the relay-plane `confirmRouteViaHopAck` path (`internal/core/node/routing_hop_ack.go`) does NOT synthesise such an entry — a `relay_hop_ack` frame carries only `(recipient, next-hop)`, neither `Origin` nor `SeqNo` are on the wire, and forging them would corrupt ranking input that split-horizon and withdrawal authority depend on. If the original triple was evicted from the bucket between the relay send and the hop_ack arrival, `confirmRouteViaHopAck` falls through with the `route_hop_ack_no_matching_route` log marker; the bucket is re-populated by subsequent announcement traffic through the normal admission rules. Cap admission via hop_ack is therefore exercised by callers that already have the full lineage (e.g. a hypothetical `route_query` response handler with authentic Origin/SeqNo metadata); the wire-only `relay_hop_ack` path stays out of cap admission by design.
- `RemoveDirectPeer.ExposedBackups` walks the surviving non-withdrawn routes and reports the destination as exposed if any of them are alive. The cap reduces the maximum number of survivors, but the boolean signal — "is at least one backup alive?" — is unaffected.

**Liveness pre-tier in eviction.** The cap eviction order is `(live > dead) → trust → hops → expiry`, with liveness as the FIRST tier. The pre-tier covers ONLY expired-but-not-withdrawn rows (`Hops < HopsInfinity` with `ExpiresAt` in the past): they are still cap-counted, and an expired hop_ack is "worse" than any live candidate regardless of trust. Withdrawn rows (`Hops = HopsInfinity`) are NOT in this comparison at all — rule 0 of the admission policy excludes them from both `bucketCount` and the eviction-search, so the cap never tries to evict a tombstone or trade it against a live candidate (see "Wire-format invariant" above for why tombstones live outside the K-counted slots). Without the live-vs-expired pre-tier, a bucket of K expired hop_acks would dominate a fresh announcement on trust alone (`hop_ack > announcement`), the announcement would be rejected as "worse than worst", and `Lookup` — which filters expired/withdrawn entries on the read side — would still return zero usable routes for the bucket until `TickTTL` reclaimed the rows. The pre-tier makes the cap drop those expired-but-not-withdrawn rows at admission time and absorb the new live entry, restoring the bucket to a usable state without waiting for `TickTTL`.

**Observability — `RouteCapStats`.** `Table.CapStats()` exposes monotonic counters for each `RouteAdmissionDecision`:

- `Accepted` — admitted into a bucket with room. Sourced exclusively from announce / hop_ack ingestion (`routeStore.AdmitNew` via `UpdateRoute`); `AddDirectPeer` deliberately does NOT bump this counter on a below-K direct registration.
- `AcceptedReplaced` — admitted by displacing the worst evictable candidate. Both announce / hop_ack ingestion (incoming row strictly better than the worst evictable) AND direct registration on a saturated bucket (direct admission cannot be rejected, so the cap evicts to make room) contribute here.
- `RejectedFull` — bucket saturated and incoming was not strictly better. Announce / hop_ack only — direct registration never lands here.
- `RejectedAllProtected` — bucket saturated with only direct/local entries. Announce / hop_ack only.

The four K-cap counters are published as part of `routing.Snapshot.CapStats` and surfaced in `fetchRouteSummary` under the `cap_admission` JSON object (key name kept for operator-facing stability — see `docs/rpc/routing.md` for the field-level semantic notes). The same JSON envelope also carries three counters belonging to independent policies: `seqno_flap_holdowns` (Phase 1 P2 — gated by `CORSA_MAX_SEQNO_ADVANCE_PER_WINDOW` + `CORSA_SEQNO_ADVANCE_WINDOW_SECONDS`), `fast_invalidations` (Phase 1 P3 — gated by `CORSA_MAX_SANE_HOPS`), and `bad_hops_holdowns` (bad-hops hysteresis — a recidivism hold-down on top of P3 that mutes per-event tombstone churn for Identities exceeding the fast-invalidation budget; reachable only when P3 itself is enabled, ENABLED by default with no env var, test/embedding opt-out via `WithMaxBadHopsPerWindow(0)`); those three are NOT silenced when the K-cap is disabled, and the K-cap counters are NOT silenced when any P2/P3/hysteresis knob is disabled — see the per-counter rows in `docs/rpc/routing.md` for the per-policy kill switches. Operators monitor `AcceptedReplaced / (Accepted + AcceptedReplaced)` as the cap eviction rate. The metric reflects cap pressure on announce / hop_ack traffic primarily — `Accepted` is reserved for that surface — with the small caveat that direct registrations against saturated buckets bump the numerator but not the denominator. On nodes with frequent direct reconnects against full buckets the rate slightly over-reads, but that is itself a form of cap pressure (a reconnect that would have appended a K+1 row without the cap). `RejectedAllProtected` is a sanity counter, not a fan-out diagnostic: a single Identity bucket can hold at most one direct entry (`Uplink` must equal the destination `Identity` for a direct claim), so the counter only advances when the protected slot in a specific Identity bucket is occupied by a direct claim and the cap leaves no other slot for the incoming non-direct candidate. With `K=1` that condition is normal — the direct row already filled the only slot — and the counter is effectively "K=1 was too tight for this destination". With `K≥2` it usually points at a test or direct-restore edge case rather than at fan-out sizing.

### Snapshot freshness

`Service.RoutingSnapshot()` (the `RoutingProvider` implementation consumed by `fetchRouteTable`, `fetchRouteSummary`, `fetchRouteLookup`, the desktop reachability indicator and the file router's per-decision `RouteSnap` callback) reads a cached `routing.Snapshot` published by the hot-reads refresher — the same infrastructure that backs `fetch_network_stats`, `fetch_peer_health`, `get_peers` and the ConnectionManager slots view. The publisher rebuilds the snapshot only when `routing.Table.ConsumeDirty()` returns true (some writer mutated the table since the previous publish), and the rebuild itself is the only place where `routing.Table.t.mu.RLock` is acquired. RPC handlers and the file router callback perform a single `atomic.Pointer.Load` and never block on the routing-table mutex.

Two distinct staleness bounds apply to the cached path:

- **Structural changes** (route accepted, withdrawn, replaced; direct peer added/removed; flap burst arming hold-down; flap-state cleanup after a writer touched the table) are reflected within one refresh interval (currently 500 ms, shared with the other hot snapshots) plus the time the publisher needs to acquire `t.mu.RLock`. The dirty-flag economy keeps the publisher cheap on a stable network: as long as no writer (`UpdateRoute` accepted path, `WithdrawRoute` success, `AddDirectPeer` for new or reactivated routes, `RemoveDirectPeer`, `InvalidateTransitRoutes` with non-zero invalidations, `TickTTL` with real expiry or flap-state mutation, `RecordSuccessfulRouteAdd` with real reset) flagged the table, the publisher's tick is a no-op CAS check. Idempotent paths (re-add of an already-active direct peer, same-SeqNo announcements with worse hops or weaker source, no-op `TickTTL` ticks) deliberately leave the flag clean.
- **Time-derived state** (`IsExpired`, `ttl_seconds`, `FlapEntry.InHoldDown`) is bounded loosely. The dirty-flag publisher only republishes when a writer touches the table, and the wall-clock timestamps that drive these fields move forward without any writer event:
  - A finite-TTL route silently ages out — no writer until `TickTTL` (every 10 s) rewrites the entry. `IsExpired(snap.TakenAt)` therefore stays false in the cached snapshot until `TickTTL` runs and republishes; worst-case lag for "route aged out" equals the `TickTTL` interval (≈10 s) plus one refresh tick (≈500 ms).
  - `fs.holdDownUntil` elapses — same shape: hold-down expiry is not a writer event. `TickTTL` clears `fs.holdDownUntil` when it observes the deadline has passed and marks the table dirty so the next refresh publishes `InHoldDown=false`. The flip from `InHoldDown=true` to `false` is therefore visible within `TickTTL` interval (≈10 s) + one refresh tick (≈500 ms), not within a single refresh tick. Hold-down arming is a writer event (the disconnect that crossed the flap threshold) and is reflected within the structural bound.

  Both `Snapshot` and `FlapSnapshot` normalize `FlapEntry.HoldDownUntil` to zero whenever `InHoldDown` is false, so consumers never see a non-zero past timestamp paired with `InHoldDown=false` even if `TickTTL` has not yet cleared `fs.holdDownUntil`.

  Time-derived bounds are acceptable for UI dashboards (operator sees a stale TTL number or a stale "in hold-down" indicator for a few seconds) but unacceptable for routing decisions that gate user-initiated actions; those paths must use a fresher view.

Under writer pressure on `t.mu` the publisher itself may stall, but every consumer continues to serve the previously published snapshot — the same starvation-resistance invariant that decoupled `fetch_network_stats` from `s.peerMu` writers in phase 1.

**Direct routing-table reads — `routing.Table.Lookup` and `routing.Table.Snapshot`.** Code that needs strictly fresh state calls the underlying table directly; that path is not exposed over RPC. Two shapes are used:

- `routing.Table.Lookup(peer)` — per-destination O(K) slice scan over only the routes for one identity (typically 1–10 entries), filtering withdrawn and expired against the table's own clock. Three production consumers share this fresh oracle:
  - `file_integration.isPeerReachable` — gates user-initiated file transfers and `file_announce` ingestion. A route added microseconds before the call (e.g. just-completed handshake) must be visible immediately, otherwise the UI flashes "peer unreachable" for half a second after a successful connect. The same callback is dispatched by the periodic `FileTransferManager` tick for every active transfer under `m.mu`, so paying full-table snapshot cost per call would be O(transfers × routes) under the file-transfer lock — `Lookup` keeps the cost flat. The function still respects the lock discipline: the peer-domain probe (direct-session check, file-capable peer set, localID) runs under a short `s.peerMu.RLock` that is released BEFORE `Lookup` is called, so the two reads are sequential, not nested.
  - `filerouter.Router.SendFileCommand` (locally-originated send path) — wired through `RouterConfig.RouteLookup`, the same fresh oracle. A route accepted right before the user clicks "send file" must be visible immediately on the very next pipeline step. Without the fresh path the user would observe a 0–500 ms window where `isPeerReachable` reports the destination as reachable but `SendFileCommand` returns "no route to <dst>" because the cached snapshot has not yet republished after the dirty-flag CAS.
  - `filerouter.Router.ExplainRoute` (diagnostic surface) — uses the same `RouteLookup` so the planner output mirrors what the live `SendFileCommand` would actually do. If the diagnostic and the live send read different sources, an operator staring at `explainFileRoute` output during the cached snapshot's republish window would see a path the live send cannot use (or vice versa).
- `routing.Table.Snapshot()` — full deep copy of the routing table under `t.mu.RLock`. Used by integration tests in `internal/core/node` and `internal/core/routing` that mutate the table and immediately verify the result. Production code should prefer `Lookup` whenever the question is "what does the table say about peer X right now"; only call `Snapshot` when the consumer genuinely needs the full table, and never on a hot per-decision path.

The `RouteSnap` callback handed to the file router still uses the cached path, but only for the **transit** forwarding inside `HandleInbound`: an in-flight frame already carries its own metadata, the router consults the table on every relay decision, and paying full snapshot cost per call would dominate transit latency. The router's transit decision is best-effort: TTL, split-horizon and capability filters are applied during candidate collection (`collectRouteCandidates`) before the send attempt; the send loop itself only calls `sessionSend` and does not re-read the table on the socket-write path. The locally-originated counterpart (`collectFreshRouteCandidates`) feeds the same filter+rank kernel from `RouteLookup`, so transit and locally-originated paths agree on the comparator/dedup contract for any given input set — they only differ in where the per-destination route slice comes from.

**Caveat — `fetchRouteTable` next-hop enrichment.** `Service.RoutingSnapshot()` itself is fully lock-free, but the `routeTableHandler` that consumes it additionally calls `RoutingProvider.PeerTransport` for every distinct next-hop identity to enrich the response with `next_hop.address` and `next_hop.network`. The current `Service.PeerTransport` takes `s.peerMu.RLock` to walk `peerIDs` / `health` / `sessions`. A peer-domain writer storm can therefore still delay `fetchRouteTable`, even though the routing-table mutex is no longer on the critical path. `fetchRouteSummary` and `fetchRouteLookup` do not call `PeerTransport` and remain fully lock-free. Migrating `PeerTransport` onto a cached peer-transport view is tracked separately and is out of scope for this phase.

### Known limitations

**Full integration tests (pending).** Unit tests cover individual components. Integration tests for 5-node shortest path selection, withdrawal propagation timing, reconnect with different identity, and rapid disconnect/reconnect loop convergence are pending and should be completed before real-world rollout.

**Announcement frame size cap (implemented).** `SendAnnounceRoutes` and `SendRoutesUpdate` paginate their payload through `chunkAnnounceEntriesBySize` so each emitted `announce_routes` / `routes_update` frame is independently size-checked against `protocol.MaxFrameLine = 128 KiB` (the writer-side budget mirrored on the receive side by `maxCommandLineBytes`). The chunker greedily packs entries into a chunk and pre-marshals the candidate frame after each addition; when the candidate would cross the budget, the chunk is flushed and the new entry starts a fresh chunk. Oversize inputs are therefore split into ordered consecutive frames; the receive side merges them into the same logical update without any wire-format change, since each frame is independently valid. Single entries whose own marshaled form already exceeds the budget (e.g. an entry carrying an oversized `Extra` blob) are reported via the chunker's `skipped` return and dropped with the `announce_routes_entry_oversize_dropped` metric — the remaining entries still ship. Without this cap, a node with a large table could push a single oversize frame, the receiver's line-size guard would close the connection with `frame-too-large`, the sender would mark the peer disconnected and immediately redial, and both sides would enter a reconnect storm. Pacing/jitter and per-peer rate limiting remain as separate items.

**Routing loops (Iteration 1 risk).** Split horizon and withdrawal semantics reduce simple loop scenarios. However, the current design has no path vector, no poisoned reverse, and hop-limit applies to message relay TTL, not to DV convergence. For the Iteration 1 MVP, split horizon + withdrawal + flap dampening is considered the minimum viable loop prevention. Flap dampening (hold-down timer) prevents rapid disconnect/reannounce sequences from creating convergence oscillations. If integration tests  reveal loopy behavior, a fix must land in Iteration 1, not be deferred. Potential further mitigations: triggered withdrawal propagation latency bounds, or path recording in a future iteration.

**No global lookup.** Distance vector gives each node knowledge only about destinations reachable via its neighbors. There is no mechanism to discover an arbitrary identity in the network if no neighbor has advertised a route to it. This is not a defect — it is the fundamental boundary of the DV approach. If "find any user in the network" is needed, it requires a separate discovery/query layer (e.g., DHT in Iteration 4, or a dedicated lookup service). The routing table is not the right place for global search, and no patch to it will solve the problem.

### Wire format

The `announce_routes` frame is the legacy v1 announce-plane frame. It carries a list of route entries; only fields needed for convergence are transmitted on the wire. TTL and Source are derived locally.

```json
{
  "type": "announce_routes",
  "routes": [
    {"identity": "alice_fp", "origin": "bob_fp", "hops": 1, "seq": 42},
    {"identity": "carol_fp", "origin": "dave_fp", "hops": 16, "seq": 18}
  ]
}
```

A withdrawal is simply a route with `hops: 16` and an incremented `seq`.

The `routes_update` frame is the v2 delta frame. Its payload shape is identical to `announce_routes` — same `routes` array, same entry fields — but its `type` is `routes_update`. Semantically the difference is strict: `routes_update` carries ONLY entries that have changed since the receiver's baseline, and it is NEVER sent as the first sync after session establishment. Each entry's rules (`hops=16` + new `seq` = withdrawal, origin-only wire withdrawal, etc.) match the legacy frame exactly. A receiver that applied the delta without a baseline would be unable to distinguish "peer has no other routes" from "peer has routes it didn't include this time", so the sender MUST first establish a self-contained baseline (`announce_routes` for v1/v2 peers or `route_announce_v3` with `kind="full"` for v3-triplet peers — see First-sync wire-frame invariant).

The `request_resync` frame is a v2 control frame with no payload. It is emitted by a receiver when a delta (`routes_update` or `route_announce_v3` with `kind="delta"`) arrives before any baseline for the current session — an unanchored delta. On arrival it triggers `AnnounceStateRegistry.MarkInvalid(peer)` plus `AnnounceLoop.TriggerUpdate()`, so the next cycle's forced-full branch re-delivers the baseline in whichever format the peer can accept (legacy `announce_routes` for v1/v2 peers, or `route_announce_v3` with `kind="full"` for v3-triplet peers — `sendFullAnnounce` dispatches between `sendLegacyFull` and `sendV3Full` based on the peer's negotiated cap set, per the first-sync invariant). The frame has no `routes` field; its mere arrival is the signal.

```json
{"type": "request_resync"}
```

### Capability gating

The `mesh_routing_v1` capability is advertised during the handshake. Only peers with this capability in their negotiated set will receive `announce_routes` frames. Legacy peers continue to function via gossip without disruption.

The `mesh_routing_v2` capability is an opt-in refinement on top of `mesh_routing_v1`. A peer negotiates v2 to declare that it understands `routes_update` (v2 delta) and `request_resync` (v2 control). v2 picks up only on the FULL v2 triplet `mesh_routing_v1` + `mesh_routing_v2` + `mesh_relay_v1` (see `classifyDeltaMode` / `hasCapV2Triplet` in `internal/core/routing/announce.go`). Relay is part of the triplet because the send-side dispatch in `dispatchAnnouncePlaneFrameWithCaps` gates `SendRoutesUpdate` on it — a relay-less v2 classification would route to a sender that refuses the frame with no legacy fallback (Round-21 alignment, mirror of the v3 triplet for `route_announce_v3`). v1 is the floor: a peer that advertises `mesh_routing_v2` without `mesh_routing_v1` is treated as v1-only, because the first-sync invariant (`announce_routes` baseline, or `route_announce_v3 kind="full"` for v3-triplet peers) is gated on v1 and a peer that cannot receive a baseline cannot consume a delta. Mode selection for the delta path is driven by the per-cycle `AnnounceTarget.Capabilities` from the session selected by the announce loop; the persistent `AnnouncePeerState.capabilities` record is reconciled to that snapshot at cycle start (see "Announce delta mode selection" below). No persistent `Mode` field is stored on `AnnouncePeerState`.

Phase 2 introduces two additional capabilities, both advertised by default:

- `mesh_route_probe_v1` — gates the `route_probe_v1` / `route_probe_ack_v1` pair (active reachability probes). Probes are scheduled every `HealthProbeInterval` (30 s) for `(Identity, Uplink)` pairs in the `Questionable` health state. Verify-before-trust for a previously unseen uplink is implemented by seeding the freshly admitted pair as `Questionable` so the next 30 s probe tick picks it up; there is no immediate one-shot probe at admission time. Each tick emits at most `maxProbesPerTick` probes; when a node holds more `Questionable` pairs than that, the excess are deferred to later ticks and converge via the passive hop-ack timeline (122 s) instead of the active path — so the ~90 s active-detection figure holds only while the live `Questionable` set is within the per-tick budget.
- `mesh_route_query_v1` — gates the `route_query_v1` / `route_query_response_v1` pair (on-demand single-hop route lookup). Used for fast recovery when all known uplinks for a target identity transition to `Bad` or `Dead`. Per-target rate limit: three emissions per 30 s sliding window. Fan-out targets must advertise the FULL triplet `mesh_route_query_v1 + mesh_relay_v1 + mesh_routing_v1` — a `mesh_route_query_v1`-only peer cannot serve as a transit next-hop for the ingested response, so the sender filters candidates accordingly (`peersWithRouteQueryCap` in `internal/core/node/routing_query_sender.go`).

Mixed-version interop. Phase 2 capabilities are independent and additive at the wire layer, but the local health-store side-effects of route admission run unconditionally on the receiver for LEARNED claims: every accepted learned `(Identity, Uplink)` claim is seeded as `Questionable` in `RouteHealthState` regardless of the announcing peer's capability set, and the passive idle timeline (`Good` → `Questionable` → `Bad` → `Dead`) ages every entry. Direct (own-origin, `Identity == Uplink`) claims are the exception: `AddDirectPeer` seeds them as `HealthGood` because the session-establishment handshake is the proof of liveness, and `TickHealth` skips Direct pairs entirely because their lifecycle is session-bound (`AddDirectPeer` / `RemoveDirectPeer`) rather than traffic-driven. A quiet direct peer therefore stays `Good` for the lifetime of the session even without organic hop_ack traffic; operators should not expect a healthy direct peer to decay through the passive timeline. A `mesh_routing_v1`-only peer therefore still produces health entries on our side; what it skips is active probe traffic (no `mesh_route_probe_v1` → `peerSendableConnectionsLocked` filters the session out before `sendProbe` reaches `Register` — see `internal/core/node/routing_probe_loop.go::sendProbe` for the capability gate) and the query fan-out (no `mesh_route_query_v1` → not eligible as fan-out target, see `peersWithRouteQueryCap` in `internal/core/node/routing_query_sender.go`). `Lookup` still ranks routes by `CompositeScore`, so a never-probed learned pair stays at `Questionable` and ranks below confirmed alternatives — the same way as any other `Questionable` pair. Full protocol details live in `docs/protocol/route_health.md`.

### Route health and composite scoring

Phase 2 of the cluster-mesh plan enriches `routing.Table.Lookup` with active quality signals: per-`(Identity, Uplink)` health state, RTT EWMA, and a single composite-score ranking function that replaces the legacy by-hops sort. The signals are local — the zero-trust budget forbids trusting RTT or health attestations from remote peers (RTT is always measured from the sender's own probe round-trip; health labels never travel on the wire). Full wire-protocol contract and state-machine transitions live in `docs/protocol/route_health.md`; this section summarises the routing-side surface.

`RouteHealthState` lives in `routing.Table` under `t.mu` (see `docs/locking.md` "Cluster-mesh Phase 2 — routing.Table.mu ownership of RouteHealthState"). The pair `(Identity, Uplink)` is the storage key — the same key the post-Phase-1 `UplinkClaim` storage uses, so health entries naturally co-evolve with their underlying claims. The state machine drives four levels:

| State | Trigger to enter | Lookup semantic |
|---|---|---|
| `Good` | `relay_hop_ack` received OR `route_probe_ack_v1(reachable=true)` arrived | Full composite score, no penalty. |
| `Questionable` | hop-ack idle > 60 s | Penalty `scoreHealthQPenalty` (−250); probe scheduled every 30 s (at most `maxProbesPerTick` per tick — excess pairs converge via the passive 122 s path). Strict-tier ordering keeps every Questionable below every Good. |
| `Bad` | hop-ack idle > 122 s OR 3 consecutive probe failures | Penalty `scoreHealthBadPenalty` (−500); selectable only as last resort. Strict-tier ordering keeps every Bad below every Questionable (and therefore every Good). The TableRouter relay path treats "selected Bad" as the recovery trigger for `route_query_v1`. |
| `Dead` | hop-ack idle > 182 s | Excluded from Lookup AND from announce projection. Exception for `RouteSourceDirect`: Direct (own-origin) claims are session-bound, kept selectable with the `Bad`-equivalent penalty (`scoreHealthBadPenalty`) instead of the excluded sentinel — see `docs/protocol/route_health.md`. |

The active (probe-driven) and passive (hop-ack-driven) timelines are asymmetric on purpose: active checks should detect failure faster than passive observation (~90 s vs ~122 s for the `Bad` transition).

RTT is tracked as an exponentially weighted moving average with α=0.3. The primary sample source is the active probe round-trip (sender-measured at `route_probe_v1` send → `route_probe_ack_v1` receive via `probeRegistry.Resolve`). `Table.MarkHopAck` / `Table.ConfirmHopAck` accept a non-zero `rtt` argument for future plumbing, but the production hop-ack receive path in `internal/core/node/routing_hop_ack.go::confirmRouteViaHopAck` currently passes `rtt=0` because the original relay send timestamp is not threaded through the relay pipeline; `rtt=0` preserves the prior EWMA value untouched, so the field never carries a forged sample. The responder's `rtt_ms` payload is informational only — the sender ALWAYS uses its own measured round-trip for ranking, in line with the zero-trust budget.

`CompositeScore(hops, source, health)` is the unified ranking function. Higher is better. The formula:

```
score = 100 − hops × 10
      + rttBonus(health.RTT)         // +30 at RTT ≤ 20 ms, linear taper to 0 at 100 ms
      + healthPenalty(health.Health) // 0/−250/−500 for Good/Questionable/Bad; sentinel −1 for Dead (strict-tier ordering)
      + sourceBonus(source)          // +20 Direct/Local, +10 HopAck, 0 Announcement
```

`Lookup` filters out `Dead` claims and sorts the rest by descending score. Phase 3 extended the formula with the reliability term documented in "Reputation, multi-path failover, and black-hole cooldown" below; it folds into the same `CompositeScore` additively.

Nil-health safe: when a pair has no health entry yet (cold-start), the formula skips the RTT and health terms and falls back to `base + sourceBonus`. This reproduces the pre-Phase-2 `isBetter` ordering modulo trust-tier ties, keeping backward-compatibility for callers that have not yet observed any health-driving traffic.

### Reputation, multi-path failover, and black-hole cooldown

Phase 3 of the cluster-mesh plan layers a local hop-ack reputation surface on top of the Phase 2 health-state machine. Same key (`(Identity, Uplink)`), same lock (`routing.Table.t.mu`), same trust budget (zero-trust — third-party complaints are NEVER accepted as reputation evidence; only observations made by this node count). Wire-protocol contract and the engineering decisions behind the constants live in `docs/cluster-mesh/phase-3-multipath-reputation.md`; this section summarises the routing-side surface.

**Reputation primitives.** Each `RouteHealthState` carries five reputation fields next to the Phase 2 health-state machine:

- `HopAckAttempts` / `HopAckSuccesses` — raw counters that survive past process restart only in memory (reputation is NOT persisted; Phase 3 §4.9 decision #6).
- `ReliabilityScore` — EWMA of binary hop-ack outcomes (α=0.2). Cold-start: the first observation seeds the score directly. Below `ReliabilityWarmupSamples=3` attempts the score is ignored by `CompositeScore` to avoid letting a single observation flip ranking.
- `ConsecutiveFailures` — current failure streak; reset on any organic success.
- `CooldownUntil` — non-zero deadline of an armed black-hole cooldown (see below).

`CompositeScore` adds a `reliabilityBonus` term of `±ReliabilityBonusMax` (±20) symmetric around `ReliabilityScore=0.5`. The magnitude is sized below the health-tier penalty (`scoreHealthQPenalty=250`) so the strict-tier ordering `Good ≻ Questionable ≻ Bad` survives any reliability extreme — release-blocking invariant pinned by `TestCompositeScore_ReliabilityBonusPreservesStrictTier_*`.

**Multi-path failover.** When a forwarded `relay_message` does not produce a `relay_hop_ack` within `defaultHopAckBudgetSeconds=10`, the relay state store fires `Service.onRelayHopAckTimeout`. The handler records the failure via `routing.Table.MarkHopFailure` AND attempts to re-send the same wire frame through the highest-ranked alternative uplink (skipping the failed peer, the previous-hop sender, and any address already in `AbandonedForwardedTo`). Bounded by `MaxFailoverRetries=1` so the worst-case per-message latency stays at `~2 × defaultHopAckBudgetSeconds` before gossip fallback / periodic `retryRelayDeliveries` takes over. The original frame is stashed on `relayForwardState.FrameLine` at forward time so any hop in the relay chain can retry, not just the origin.

**Multi-path traffic shaping.** `Table.LookupForRelay(identity, hint)` wraps the plain `Lookup` and occasionally rotates the top-ranked candidate onto an alternative when the favourite is under-observed (warmup: `HopAckAttempts < ReliabilityShapingMinAttempts=10`) or has just exited cooldown (`LastCooldownClearedAt` within `ShapingRecentCooldownWindow=1min`). The rotation fires roughly one in `ShapingProbeRatio=4` calls and is skipped whenever no acceptable alternative exists. An acceptable alternative must be neither a shaping candidate itself (swapping one warmup for another defers nothing) nor a Bad/Dead pair: `Lookup` keeps fully-observed `HealthBad` pairs (merely low-scored) and Direct `HealthDead` pairs (direct exemption), so `LookupForRelay` applies its own tier gate (`isShapingAlternativeAcceptable` — Good/Questionable only) to avoid diverting traffic from a merely-warming Good candidate onto a known-worse path. The goal is to accelerate sample accrual, not to redistribute traffic among uniformly under-observed or unhealthy paths. The hint is a monotonic per-`Service` counter (`Service.nextRelayShapingHint()`) so the rotation cadence stays deterministic across concurrent relay forwards.

**Black-hole cooldown.** After `BlackHoleThreshold=5` consecutive hop-ack failures the apply method arms `CooldownUntil = now + BlackHoleCooldown` (2 minutes). The Lookup, AnnounceTo, AnnounceTargetFor, and Announceable paths all suppress claims with an active cooldown — same suppression as `HealthDead` but auto-clearing once the deadline elapses (via `Table.TickHealth.applyCooldownExpiryLocked`). Unlike the `HealthDead` filter the cooldown gate has NO Direct exemption: a Direct pair that reliably misses hop-acks IS a black hole regardless of the session being alive, and suppressing it from Lookup matches the empirical signal reputation already recorded. Pinned by `TestBlackHole_DirectClaimNotExempt`.

**Incremental sync via table digest.** The `route_sync_digest_v1` / `route_sync_summary_v1` wire pair (gated by `mesh_route_sync_v1`, see `docs/protocol/route_sync.md` for the full contract) lets a peer that reconnects within `SessionDigestCacheTTL=5min` short-circuit the reconnect forced full sync when both sides agree their `(Identity, MaxSeqNo)` views match. The reconnect full sync is the path this targets: on reconnect the session hook arms a short pending suppression window (`MarkPeerDigestPending`) before its `TriggerUpdate`, so the immediate cycle holds off until the summary lands; a match extends it for one forced-full cadence via `MarkPeerDigestMatched`, a mismatch clears it via `ClearPeerDigestSuppression`. The suppression window length is owned by the announce loop (`EffectiveForcedFullSyncInterval`), not the wire handler. The digest is a local hint — a mismatched (or absent) reply only loses one forced-full-sync window, and the announce plane remains the authoritative source of routing state. The gate suppresses a SOFT (session-boundary / reconnect) resync — `view.ResyncIsHard == false` — but never the first-ever initial sync (`LastSentSnapshot == nil`) nor a HARD resync (`request_resync` / consistency-loss `MarkInvalid`, `ResyncIsHard == true`).

**RPC observability.** `fetchRouteReputation` surfaces the reputation fields as a structured snapshot — same shape conventions as `fetchRouteHealth` so a UI can join the two by `(identity, uplink)`. Pure read; never triggers a probe, digest, MarkHopFailure, or any other side effect. See `docs/rpc/routing.md` for the wire schema.

Capability requirements for a table-directed relay next-hop depend on the role of the next-hop peer:

- **Destination (hops=1):** The next-hop IS the final recipient. Only `mesh_relay_v1` is required — the peer must accept `relay_message` frames but does not need to forward further.
- **Transit (hops>1):** The next-hop must forward the message onward using its own routing table. Both `mesh_relay_v1` (accept relay) and `mesh_routing_v1` (table-directed forwarding) are required.

A directly connected relay-only peer (no `mesh_routing_v1`) is still usable as a destination via table-directed delivery. Requiring both capabilities for all next-hops would drop direct delivery to relay-only peers and unnecessarily degrade to blind gossip. `resolveRouteNextHopAddress` in `node/routing_relay.go` enforces this distinction.

### Announce delta mode selection

For each routing-capable peer, every announce cycle derives the delta wire frame at cycle start. The classifier reads two capability snapshots that are reconciled at cycle entry:

- **`AnnounceTarget.Capabilities`** — per-cycle immutable snapshot captured by `routingCapablePeers` under the same `s.peerMu.RLock` that produced `Address` and `Identity`. This reflects what the session `routingCapablePeers` selected as the announce target reports at this cycle's tick.
- **`AnnouncePeerState.capabilities`** — persistent per-peer record. Reconciled to the target snapshot at the start of every per-peer goroutine via `AnnounceStateRegistry.UpdateCapabilities`. After the sync the persistent record is a derived view of the same session selected as `AnnounceTarget`.

Reconciling at cycle start makes `classifyDeltaMode` read two agreeing snapshots in production: by the time the function runs, the persistent record has just been overwritten with the target caps. The two-input shape is preserved as a defensive net — see "Persistent caps as a derived view of the chosen target" above for the divergence-path rationale.

Classification rules (implemented in `classifyDeltaMode`, `internal/core/routing/announce.go`):

- both inputs contain the FULL v2 triplet `mesh_routing_v1` + `mesh_routing_v2` + `mesh_relay_v1` → **v2 delta** via `SendRoutesUpdate` (`routes_update` wire frame). Relay is part of the triplet because the send-side dispatch in `dispatchAnnouncePlaneFrameWithCaps` gates `SendRoutesUpdate` on the same triplet — a relay-less v2 classification would route to a sender that refuses the frame with no legacy fallback (Round-21 alignment, mirror of the v3 triplet for `route_announce_v3`);
- neither input contains the full triplet (missing v2, missing v1, OR missing relay) → **v1 delta** via `SendAnnounceRoutes` (`announce_routes` wire frame);
- inputs disagree on v2 → **divergence**: `MarkInvalid(peer)` + legacy delta for this cycle; next cycle runs forced-full through `SendAnnounceRoutes`. With cycle-time reconciliation in place this branch is unreachable from the loop and serves only as a defensive fallback for any future code path that bypasses `UpdateCapabilities`.

Forced-full and connect-time paths are NOT subject to this delta-mode classification. They always emit a self-contained baseline frame — `SendAnnounceRoutes` for v1/v2 peers, or `SendRouteAnnounceV3` with `kind="full"` for peers that negotiated the v3 triplet. Neither path ever picks a delta frame (`SendRoutesUpdate` or `kind="delta"`), because a delta cannot bootstrap a session. See the First-sync wire-frame invariant for the full contract; the v3 baseline branch lives in `sendV3Full` (`internal/core/routing/announce.go`) and the connect-time v3 branch in `sendConnectTimeFullSync` (`internal/core/node/routing_announce.go`).

**Send-time capability gate with captured-handle dispatch.** Mode classification runs against the per-cycle `AnnounceTarget` snapshot. Between that snapshot and the actual write inside `SendRoutesUpdate` / `SendRequestResync`, the underlying session at the announce address can close and be replaced by a session that does NOT hold the gate the receive dispatcher requires (or be torn down outright). Putting v2 wire bytes on such a narrower session is a protocol violation: the receiver rejects the frame and may ban the sender. The send path closes the race via `Service.dispatchAnnouncePlaneFrameWithCaps`, which captures the live transport handle (sendCh for outbound sessions, ConnID for inbound conns) under the same `peerMu` RLock as the cap validation, then writes to the captured handle outside the lock. Capturing the handle — not just the cap snapshot — is the load-bearing piece: ConnID is monotonic and never reused, so a replacement inbound conn at the same `remoteAddr` has its own fresh ConnID and never receives our bytes; outbound `peerSession.sendCh` is owned by exactly one session, so a replacement session at the same address has its own sendCh that we never touch. `peerMu` is released before any blocking I/O, matching the CLAUDE.md prohibition on holding domain mutexes across network I/O.

The cap predicate each v2 sender enforces matches its receive-dispatcher contract:
- `SendRoutesUpdate` requires `mesh_routing_v1` AND `mesh_routing_v2` AND `mesh_relay_v1` — the same gate `routingCapablePeers` uses to pick `AnnounceTarget` candidates (v1+relay) plus the v2 capability the announce loop additionally requires for the v2 path. Both inbound (`service.go`) and session (`peer_management.go`) dispatchers gate `routes_update` on the same triple, so a narrower replacement session — v2 alone, or v1+v2 without relay — would have its `routes_update` rejected on receive anyway, and the send gate stops it earlier.
- `SendRequestResync` requires `mesh_routing_v2` only. The receive dispatchers gate `request_resync` on v2 alone (it carries no payload, just signals "clear my announce state"); widening the send gate to v1+v2+relay would have the sender skip a recovery control frame that the receiver would still accept, leaving v2-only sessions permanently desynced.

On gate failure or capture miss the senders return false; the caller's per-peer announce cache stays untouched, so the next cycle re-classifies on the current session and either takes the v1 path or skips the peer entirely. Legacy `SendAnnounceRoutes` does NOT have a symmetric capture-write helper today: the same race exists in principle, but routing-capable peers always advertise `mesh_routing_v1` (the gate `routingCapablePeers` enforces), and the legacy frame is also what the first-sync invariant uses for forced-full / connect-time / divergence-fallback paths whose wider scope of mock test fixtures complicates a uniform check; if a regression triggers the v1-side race in production, the symmetric capture-and-write belongs next to the v2 senders.

### Baseline gate on v2 receive

A delta frame (v2 `routes_update` OR v3 `route_announce_v3` with `kind="delta"`) is a diff against the self-contained baseline delivered for the current session. Both receive-side handlers (`handleRoutesUpdate` and the delta branch of `handleRouteAnnounceV3`) enforce this through the same per-peer flag `AnnouncePeerState.hasReceivedBaseline`:

- on session establishment / reconnect, the flag is cleared by `MarkReconnected`;
- EITHER a legacy `announce_routes` arrival OR a `route_announce_v3` arrival with `kind="full"` sets the flag via `MarkBaselineReceived` (the legacy path runs through `applyAnnounceEntries`; the v3 full path sets it inside `handleRouteAnnounceV3` after the epoch / cap checks);
- a delta arrival (`routes_update` or `kind="delta"`) checks the flag: if unset, the receiver emits `request_resync` to the peer and drops the delta without touching the routing table; if set, the delta is applied entry-by-entry through the same `applyAnnounceEntries` core used by the baseline path.

The baseline flag is an explicit `bool` rather than a derived "do we have any entries from this peer" check: the flag is set strictly by an actual baseline-frame arrival, including an arrival with an empty entry payload — `applyAnnounceEntries` runs to completion regardless of `len(wireRoutes)`, so if an empty `announce_routes` (or an empty v3 `kind="full"`) frame is ever received it still flips `hasReceivedBaseline` via `MarkBaselineReceived` before returning. This matters for forward compatibility with peers that ship an empty baseline as an empty wire frame; without explicit flag tracking, deriving the baseline from "do we have entries" would force every subsequent delta from such a peer into a resync cycle. In this build the local send-side empty-baseline short-circuit emits NO wire frame at all (it records a local successful baseline via `RecordFullSyncSuccess` and returns without calling the wire sender), so a peer talking to this build never observes anything from us in that case and its `hasReceivedBaseline` stays false. That asymmetry is exactly why `wireBaselineSentToPeer` (v2) and `wireBaselineV3SentToPeer` (v3) exist on the send side: each stays false through its respective no-wire empty-baseline path so the next non-empty cycle is forced onto legacy `announce_routes` to actually establish a baseline on the wire — see "Empty-baseline + delta receive-gate interaction" above.

Duplicate baseline arrivals are harmless: the flag is already set and is simply re-set on each baseline-frame arrival (legacy `announce_routes` or v3 `kind="full"`).

### Phase 4 — Compact wire frames, attested links, poison-reverse

Phase 4 (shipped 2026-05) ships a compact announce wire frame, signed announcements, an explicit single-hop poison-reverse signal, and three local-only safety primitives. Every wire-protocol addition is additive and gated behind a single flag (`CORSA_ENABLE_MESH_ROUTING_V3`). After the soak period this flag now defaults to **on**; operators can opt out with `CORSA_ENABLE_MESH_ROUTING_V3=0` (or `false`/`no`/`off`) to drop the node back to the legacy v1/v2 wire path. Negotiation stays backward compatible either way — v3 frames are only sent to peers that also advertise the capability.

Wire-protocol additions (capability-gated, opt-in via the flag above):

- **`mesh_routing_v3` + `route_announce_v3`** — compact announce frame that drops the redundant `Origin` field (the receiver derives the uplink from the sending session, so `Origin` carries no routing-relevant information after the Phase 1 per-uplink storage refactor). A single frame type carries both full sync and delta via the `kind` discriminator, and a local `epoch` counter lets a receiver detect a peer table reset and force a fresh baseline. Full wire contract — `docs/protocol/route_announce_v3.md`.
- **`mesh_attested_links_v1`** — Ed25519 attestation on each `route_announce_v3` entry, signed by the destination identity's key over canonical bytes `(identity || extra)`. Hops, epoch, AND seq_no are ALL deliberately excluded so multi-hop transit verification stays correct: every per-emitter wire field (hops by receiver `+1`; epoch by sender's local table-generation counter; seq_no by transit-side outbound SeqNo synthesis that can advance past the origin's native value) would break the moment a transit node re-emits a signed entry with a restamped value. Trust ladder: verified (sig present and ed25519-verified locally) > unverified (sig present, destination pubkey unknown, OR attested-links cap not negotiated on this session) ≡ unsigned. Receive-side verification is gated on the per-session `mesh_attested_links_v1` negotiation: without the cap the sig bytes are forwarded through storage (so a downstream peer with the cap can still verify) but treated as informational locally — no entry drop on invalid, no trust bonus on success. `CompositeScore` adds a small `scoreSignedBonus = 5.0` tie-break for verified-signed claims, strictly within-tier (never rescues a Bad/Questionable pair against a Good alternative). **Production advertise is currently OFF**: `localCapabilities` does NOT include this cap, because the emit path (`route_store.AnnounceProjectionFor`) never produces an entry with `Identity == localIdentity` (the self-route is synthesised in `Lookup`/`Snapshot` but not stored), so the signer would have no input. Phase 5 anchor publication adds the self-attestation entry stream and re-enables the advertise the same day. Full wire contract — `docs/protocol/attested_links.md`.
- **`mesh_poison_reverse_v1` + `route_poison_v1`** — explicit single-hop signal a transit node sends to its direct neighbours when its uplink to an identity is lost (or its path goes dead, or a loop is detected). The receiver invalidates ONLY the `claims[identity][sender]` slot (not other uplinks, not the origin's claim — origin authority remains governed by per-Identity SeqNo monotonicity). Replaces the implicit hops=N+1 oscillation a count-to-infinity scenario produces, collapsing the bad path in one announce cycle instead of waiting TTL. Production emit hook is wired on session-close (`uplink_lost` trigger); health-dead and loop-detected triggers are incremental enhancements.

Local-only safety primitives (active by default, no wire change):

- **Rotating Bloom dedup for `s.seen`** — two filters with a 5-minute rotation cap memory regardless of message volume, trading the legacy map's perfect recall for a < 0.1% false-positive rate (0.046% at 10k keys per filter, 0.32% at 20k). Honest trade-off: a Bloom false positive at the `storeIncomingMessage` gate drops a NEW message silently — it is not "harmless dedup of an already-delivered message". The downstream effect depends on path: gossip-fanned messages still reach the recipient via any neighbour whose filter does not collide on the same id (FP events across nodes are statistically independent, so end-to-end loss rounds to zero across realistic fan-out); transit relays inject another copy through gossip as well; ONLY the direct `push_message` peer-to-peer DM path has no recovery channel — a Bloom FP there is real loss, owned by the sender-side delivery-receipt + retry layer rather than the dedup layer. False negatives are bounded by the rotation window: a key Add'd at *t* survives until at least *t* + rotation and at most *t* + 2·rotation. The downstream `MessageStore` is idempotent by `msg.ID`, so a false-negative duplicate is collapsed there without surfacing a duplicate to the user. See `internal/core/node/bloom_dedup.go` for the full discussion.
- **Per-peer announce rate limit** — token bucket per `PeerIdentity` on all received announce-plane frames (`announce_routes`, `routes_update`, `route_announce_v3`, `request_resync`, `route_poison_v1`), budgeted by ROUTE ENTRY COUNT (Round-10 fix: announce frames charge `max(1, len(entries))` tokens, control frames charge 1) and sized for legitimate chunked full-sync traffic (~10 000 route burst, 200 routes/s refill — full burst replenishes in ~50 s). Shared across wire generations so a peer cannot dodge the throttle by flipping wire generations OR by switching from announce frames to poison flood (poison tokens are charged BEFORE the base64+ed25519 verify and `Table.InvalidateUplinkClaim` mutation). The earlier per-frame budget (30-frame burst) silently truncated chunked full-syncs past ~3 000 routes — sender thought delivery succeeded and updated baseline/cache, receiver dropped the rest without feedback until the next forced-full cadence; the route-count budget makes the bound match the actual per-entry work and lets a legitimate full-sync clear in one burst. Defence against DoS from a flooding peer. See `internal/core/node/announce_ratelimit.go`.
- **100-route per-frame cap** — hard cap on the number of route entries any single announce-plane frame can carry (`maxRoutesPerAnnounceFrame = 100`), independent of the existing `MaxFrameLine` byte budget. Bounds per-frame receive work. Enforced on BOTH ends of the wire: the send-side chunkers (`chunkAnnounceEntriesBySize`, `chunkRouteAnnounceV3EntriesBySize`) split larger snapshots into ≤100-entry frames, and the receive-side handlers (`handleAnnounceRoutes`, `handleRoutesUpdate`, `handleRouteAnnounceV3`) drop the WHOLE frame when a remote peer (buggy or hostile) packs more entries than the cap allows — partial truncation would let a peer silently hide entries past the cap and would mask the misbehaviour, so the entire frame is rejected with a structured log line and the next periodic announce cycle re-syncs cleanly.

Anti-poisoning admission rule (Phase 4 §3.6): a draft "Announcement cannot override fresh Direct/HopAck" rule was investigated and found to be subsumed by the Phase 1 per-(Identity, Uplink) storage refactor — cross-uplink poisoning is structurally impossible after the refactor, and same-uplink "downgrades" are the legitimate forced-full-sync TTL refresh path documented elsewhere in this file. No code change landed for §3.6; the finding is recorded inline in `route_store_mutation.go` and `anti_poison_test.go`.

### Queue-state persistence contract (DEPRECATED — disk persistence removed)

> **Status:** queue-state disk persistence is **removed**. The contract below
> describes the now-DORMANT mechanism, retained for a few releases before full
> deletion. At runtime nothing is written to `queue-<port>.json`: the background
> persister is constructed but its `Run` goroutine is **never started**, so
> `s.queuePersist.MarkDirty()` only sets a flag and a non-blocking wake on a
> channel with no consumer — a complete no-op. The file is **deleted on
> startup** (a one-shot migration loads any pre-upgrade file once — trimming
> each peer queue to `CORSA_PENDING_RING_SIZE` — then removes it). Pending
> frames are now bounded by an in-memory per-peer ring (evict-oldest); relay
> state, receipts and outbound status live in RAM only and **do not survive a
> restart**. Rationale: the persisted JSON file was the dominant
> allocation-churn / memory source at scale, and store-and-forward is only
> required for the node's uptime — a restarted relay re-learns paths and
> senders retry end-to-end. See `docs/protocol/relay.md` INV-8.

Historically, every routing-driven mutation that had to survive a restart — `trackRelayMessage`, `trackRelayReceipt`, `noteRelayAttempt`, `queuePeerFrame`, outbound status transitions, route-drain outbound cleanup — signalled persistence via `s.queuePersist.MarkDirty()` after releasing `s.mu`. A single background goroutine owned by `queueStatePersister` (`internal/core/node/queue_state_persister.go`) observed the wake signal, debounced for 200 ms, took an `s.mu.RLock` snapshot via `queueStateSnapshotLocked`, and wrote the file atomically through `saveQueueState` (temp-file + rename). **None of this runs anymore** — the `MarkDirty` calls remain at the mutation sites only so the mechanism can be re-enabled or cleanly deleted later.

The historical contract (no longer in force):

- **Hot-path mutation sites must not call `queueStateSnapshotLocked` or `saveQueueState` directly.** They call `MarkDirty` only. (Still true structurally, but `MarkDirty` is now a no-op.)
- **The snapshot ran under `RLock`, never `Lock`.** This decoupling still matters for the live read paths: the Desktop hot RPC ticks — `fetch_network_stats`, `fetch_peer_health`, `get_peers`, `fetchRouteTable`/`fetchRouteSummary`/`fetchRouteLookup` — are decoupled from `s.mu` and `routing.Table.t.mu` entirely via five independent atomic-pointer snapshots (`networkStatsSnapshot`, `peerHealthSnapshot`, `peersExchangeSnapshot`, `cmSlotsSnapshot`, `routingSnapshot`) refreshed by a shared `hotReadsRefreshLoop`. The cmSlots snapshot caches `ConnectionManager.Slots()`; the routing snapshot caches `routing.Table.Snapshot()` gated by a dirty flag so an idle node skips the rebuild. Each snapshot is rebuilt by its own goroutine with its own ticker so a slow rebuild in one path does not delay the others.
- **Save errors re-armed the dirty flag and the wake channel** so the next loop iteration retried. (No writes occur now, so this path is inert; `ErrQueuePersistFailed` / `errors.Is` remain only for the dormant `saveQueueState`.)
- **Graceful shutdown flushed once** before returning. (No longer wired — `Run` is not started, so there is no `finalFlush` on shutdown; `FlushSync` remains for the unit tests that exercise the dormant persister directly.)

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant M as Mutation site (Lock)
    participant P as queueStatePersister
    participant D as Disk (saveQueueState)
    M->>M: s.mu.Lock / mutate / s.mu.Unlock
    M->>P: MarkDirty (atomic + non-blocking wake)
    Note over P: debounce 200 ms, coalesce burst
    P->>P: s.mu.RLock / snapshot / s.mu.RUnlock
    P->>D: saveQueueState (atomic rename)
    D-->>P: nil or ErrQueuePersistFailed
    alt error
        P->>P: re-arm dirty + wake, retry next tick
    end
```

*Diagram: Queue-state persist flow (DORMANT — the persister `Run` goroutine is no longer started; shown for the retained-but-deprecated mechanism only).*

### Package layout

```
internal/core/routing/
    types.go                    — RouteEntry, AnnounceEntry, RouteTriple, Snapshot, RouteSource
    table.go                    — Table with all CRUD, query, disconnect, and wire-projection operations
    announce.go                 — AnnounceLoop: periodic (30s) + triggered announce sender;
                                  PeerSender interface with four wire-frame methods —
                                  SendAnnounceRoutes (legacy announce_routes; used for
                                  connect-time / forced full sync on v1/v2 peers and for v1
                                  delta), SendRoutesUpdate (v2 routes_update delta; used only
                                  when both sides negotiated mesh_routing_v1 AND
                                  mesh_routing_v2 and the per-cycle classification agrees —
                                  never for first sync), SendRouteAnnounceV3 (Phase 4 compact
                                  route_announce_v3; carries kind="full" for connect-time /
                                  forced full sync on v3-triplet peers and kind="delta" for
                                  the v3 delta path), SendRequestResync (v2 request_resync
                                  control frame emitted by the receive side when ANY delta —
                                  v2 routes_update or v3 kind="delta" — arrives before any
                                  baseline); AnnounceLoop reconciles AnnouncePeerState.capabilities
                                  to the per-cycle AnnounceTarget caps via UpdateCapabilities
                                  at the start of every per-peer goroutine so classifyDeltaMode
                                  reads two agreeing snapshots in production; the divergence
                                  outcome stays as a defensive fallback for any future caller
                                  that bypasses the cycle-time sync
    announce_builder.go         — BuildAnnounceSnapshot: 4-stage aggregation (incl. per-Identity hot-fix), AnnounceSnapshot, ComputeDelta
    announce_state.go           — AnnouncePeerState, AnnounceStateRegistry: per-peer send state lifecycle
    types_test.go               — unit tests for type invariants, validation, wire projection
    table_test.go               — unit tests for table operations and invariants
    announce_test.go            — unit tests for announce loop, triggered updates, split horizon
    announce_builder_test.go    — unit tests for aggregation, snapshot equality, delta, Extra normalization
    announce_state_test.go      — unit tests for per-peer state lifecycle, View/Record methods
    announce_loop_cache_test.go — integration tests for noop suppression, delta-only, failed send retry,
                                  rate limiting, reconnect forced full sync, withdrawal retry via delta
    announce_wire_frame_test.go — guard tests pinning the first-sync wire-frame invariant: full
                                  sync and connect-time go through a self-contained baseline
                                  frame (SendAnnounceRoutes for v1/v2 peers, SendRouteAnnounceV3
                                  with kind="full" for v3-triplet peers; never a delta); v2
                                  delta path exercises SendRoutesUpdate only when both sources
                                  agree on the full v2 triplet (v1+v2+relay) and the v2 baseline
                                  has shipped; v3 delta path exercises SendRouteAnnounceV3 with
                                  kind="delta" only when the full v3 triplet (v1+v3+relay) is
                                  negotiated AND the v3 baseline has shipped; divergence falls
                                  back to SendAnnounceRoutes and marks state invalid for the
                                  next cycle

internal/core/node/
    table_router.go              — TableRouter: routing table lookup with gossip fallback
    routing_announce.go          — announce-plane wire path: TTL loop; sender implementations on
                                   node.Service for all five announce-plane wire frames
                                   (SendAnnounceRoutes, SendRoutesUpdate, SendRequestResync,
                                   SendRouteAnnounceV3 — Phase 4 compact full/delta carrying
                                   AttestedSig per entry, and SendRoutePoison — Phase 4
                                   single-hop poison-reverse) built via buildAnnounceFrame /
                                   buildRouteAnnounceV3Frame / MarshalRoutePoisonFrame and
                                   dispatched through two complementary helpers — legacy
                                   sendAnnouncePlaneFrame (for SendAnnounceRoutes; honours the
                                   "inbound:" prefix via writeFrameToInbound vs enqueuePeerFrame)
                                   and dispatchAnnouncePlaneFrameWithCaps (for SendRoutesUpdate,
                                   SendRequestResync, SendRouteAnnounceV3 and SendRoutePoison;
                                   captures sendCh / ConnID together with capability validation
                                   under one peerMu RLock so a session-replacement race between
                                   cap check and write cannot route the frame to a narrower
                                   transport at the same address); the captured ConnID path
                                   reuses writeFrameToInboundConn extracted from writeFrameToInbound;
                                   connect-time + periodic full sync via sendConnectTimeFullSync
                                   (dispatches to SendRouteAnnounceV3 kind="full" for v3-triplet
                                   peers, otherwise SendAnnounceRoutes — neither delta);
                                   handleAnnounceRoutes and handleRoutesUpdate both funnel into the
                                   shared applyAnnounceEntries receive core (announceReceiveLegacy
                                   sets baseline, announceReceiveV2 requires baseline);
                                   handleRequestResync does MarkInvalid + TriggerUpdate so next
                                   cycle re-delivers baseline; fanoutAnnounceRoutes,
                                   triggerDrainForExposed, routingCapablePeers discovery
    routing_relay.go             — relay-plane forwarding: table-directed relay, sendFrameToAddress,
                                   sendTableDirectedRelay / sendRelayToAddress, next-hop address
                                   resolution, gossip target computation (routingTargets*,
                                   routingTargetsFiltered, executeGossipTargets), sendMessageToPeer /
                                   gossipNotice / sendNoticeToPeer (§4.4 bootstrap handshake edges —
                                   this file is the §2.9 net-import carve-out for raw writes)
    routing_resolver.go          — identity↔address resolution: resolveRoutableAddress /
                                   resolveRelayAddress / resolvePeerIdentity, capability predicates
                                   (sessionHasCap, sessionHasBothCaps), inbound-conn-key helpers
                                   (inboundConnKeyForID / inboundConnKeyFromInfo)
    routing_session.go           — session lifecycle hooks for routing: onPeerSessionEstablished /
                                   onPeerSessionClosed (direct-peer registration, disconnect
                                   withdrawal fan-out), inboundPeerIdentity, per-peer announce
                                   state registry reset on connect/disconnect
    routing_hop_ack.go           — confirmRouteViaHopAck: hop_ack-driven route confirmation
    routing_drain.go             — event-driven pending queue drain: recipientFromPendingFrame,
                                   drainPendingForIdentities (extract-attempt-return pattern),
                                   drainSendMessage
    routing_provider.go          — RoutingProvider implementation on node.Service
    table_router_test.go         — unit tests for TableRouter
    routing_integration_test.go  — integration tests covering routing_announce / routing_relay /
                                   routing_resolver / routing_session / routing_hop_ack /
                                   routing_drain (file kept historical for test-file stability;
                                   private-method assertions remain same-package)

internal/core/rpc/
    routing_commands.go          — RegisterRoutingCommands: fetch_route_table, fetch_route_summary, fetch_route_lookup
    handler_routing_test.go      — unit tests for routing RPC commands
```

---

# Таблица маршрутизации — Distance Vector с Withdrawal

Связанная документация:

- [mesh.md](mesh.md) — обзор сетевого уровня
- [roadmap.md](roadmap.md) — полный план итераций
- [protocol.md](protocol.md) — протокол передачи данных

Исходники: `internal/core/routing/types.go`, `internal/core/routing/table.go`, `internal/core/routing/announce.go`, `internal/core/node/table_router.go`, `internal/core/node/routing_announce.go`, `internal/core/node/routing_relay.go`, `internal/core/node/routing_resolver.go`, `internal/core/node/routing_session.go`, `internal/core/node/routing_hop_ack.go`, `internal/core/node/routing_drain.go`, `internal/core/node/routing_provider.go`, `internal/core/rpc/routing_commands.go`

### Обзор

Пакет routing реализует таблицу маршрутизации на основе distance-vector для mesh-сети CORSA. Заменяет слепую gossip-доставку на направленную пересылку по метрике количества хопов. Gossip остаётся fallback, когда маршрут неизвестен.

### Основные типы

`RouteEntry` — это **boundary value**, передаваемое через публичный API Table (`UpdateRoute` аргумент, `Lookup` возврат, wire ingest projection). До Phase 1 shape entry одновременно был in-storage dedup key под тройкой `(Identity, Origin, NextHop)`. Post-Phase-1 storage переехал на per-`(Identity, Uplink)` `UplinkClaim` (см. подсекцию "Модель хранения" ниже); `RouteEntry` сохраняет legacy field set на boundary'е, чтобы existing callers и wire projection не менялись, но **dedup key на storage теперь только `(Identity, Uplink)`** — поле `Origin` в `RouteEntry`, возвращённое из `Lookup`, — синтезированный маркер (`localOrigin` или fallback на destination `Identity`), не оригинальный wire-frame Origin. Оригинальный wire-frame Origin сохраняется внутренне как `UplinkClaim.LastIngressOrigin` / `SeenOriginSeqs` для mixed-version interop admission rules и никогда не re-эмитится as-is на проводе.

`AnnounceEntry` — проекция `RouteEntry` для передачи по проводу. Содержит только четыре поля из `announce_routes` фреймов (Identity, Origin, Hops, SeqNo). Создаётся через `RouteEntry.ToAnnounceEntry()` или `Table.AnnounceTo()`. На провод уходит локальное значение hops отправителя как есть — получатель делает +1 при вставке в свою таблицу (receive path).

`Table` — потокобезопасное локальное хранилище маршрутов. Владеет identity ноды (`localOrigin`) и монотонным счётчиком SeqNo по каждому destination (`seqCounters`). Публичные операции: `AddDirectPeer`, `RemoveDirectPeer`, `UpdateRoute`, `WithdrawRoute`, `RefreshDirectPeers`, `TickTTL`, `Announceable`, `AnnounceTo`, `Lookup` и `Snapshot`.

`Snapshot` — иммутабельная копия таблицы на момент времени, безопасная для чтения без блокировок.

`AddDirectPeerResult` — результат подключения peer'а: `RouteEntry`, созданный или обновлённый, и флаг `Penalized`, указывающий, что flap detection применил укороченный TTL.

`RemoveDirectPeerResult` — результат отключения peer'а: wire-ready `[]AnnounceEntry` withdrawals (SeqNo уже инкрементирован, Hops=16) для own-origin direct-маршрутов, плюс количество transit-маршрутов, молча инвалидированных локально, плюс `ExposedBackups []PeerIdentity` — identity, у которых инвалидация обнажила выживший не-withdrawn backup route (используется `onPeerSessionClosed` для запуска дрейна).

`AnnounceSnapshot` — каноническое, агрегированное, peer-specific представление записей маршрутов, готовое к передаче. Wire-shape контракт имеет два слоя — см. AnnounceSnapshot doc-comment в `internal/core/routing/announce_builder.go` для полного split'а. Production слой (`routeStore.AnnounceProjectionFor`) enforce'ит per-Identity live-winner collapse И live-vs-tombstone exclusivity: максимум ОДИН live winner per Identity, с own-direct tombstones suppress'енными когда live альтернатива есть (см. "Live-vs-tombstone exclusivity на проводе" в Ключевых инвариантах ниже). Когда live winner для Identity отсутствует — tombstone эмитится, чтобы receivers evict'ились promptly. Структурный слой (`BuildAnnounceSnapshot` сам) НЕ re-enforce'ит exclusivity — синтетические test fixtures, обходящие AnnounceProjectionFor, могут передать и live entry и tombstone для одной Identity, а ComputeDelta keys на `(Identity, IsWithdrawn)`, поэтому оба слота могут coexist для synthetic input. Записи отсортированы детерминированно по `(Identity, Hops, Origin)` — Identity ASC, live winner (Hops ≤ 15) перед tombstone (Hops = 16) внутри Identity-группы, Origin lex tie-break. Nil `*AnnounceSnapshot` означает «ни один snapshot ещё не отправлен» и семантически отличается от snapshot с нулём записей.

**Per-Identity агрегация (Phase 0.x hot-fix, 2026-05; Phase 1 storage swap финализирован, 2026-Q3).** Field-data анализ 100-нодной mesh routes.json snapshot'и показал 12.7× wire amplification: 6072 stored RouteEntry строк, 1440 `(Identity, Origin)` bucket'ов, но только 113 reachable identity'ев. Hot-fix добавил per-Identity live-winner collapse (после legacy per-`(Identity, Origin)` aggregation stage, который с тех пор удалён): выбирает min `Hops`, затем higher `SeqNo`, затем deterministic `Extra` byte order, затем deterministic `Origin` lexicographic tie-break. Phase 1 затем завершил receive-side половину: storage мигрирован на per-`(Identity, Uplink)` `UplinkClaim` shape (Origin dropped из dedup key — см. "Модель хранения" подсекцию ниже для полного контракта), поэтому on-table redundancy тоже схлопнулся с 7.6× к baseline. **Live-vs-tombstone wire exclusivity:** при наличии live winner для Identity, own-direct tombstones для этой Identity SUPPRESS'ятся на проводе (live emit уже override'ит любое prior receiver state, а emit'нувшийся trailing tombstone через outbound SeqNo synthesiser получил бы строго более высокий SeqNo чем live winner и flip'нул бы receiver в withdrawn). Tombstones DO эмитятся когда live альтернативы нет — receiver всё ещё нуждается в dead signal чтобы evict вместо ожидания TTL. Outbound wire volume per cycle падает в ~12.7× в typical case (без tombstones); на disconnect events одна дополнительная запись per affected Identity ride'ится рядом КОГДА no live backup exists. Backward compat: legacy peer'ы продолжают получать `(Identity, Origin, Hops, SeqNo)` кадры с `Origin = localOrigin` (sender-originated semantic — соответствует их per-`(Identity, Origin, NextHop)` triple shape на storage); наш вклад в их storage drops с N записей per `(Identity, Origin)` lineage до (1 live winner OR 1 tombstone) per Identity, и SeqNo timeline который они наблюдают — синтезированный per-`(Identity, sender)` shape из outbound SeqNo helpers.

`AnnouncePeerState` — per-peer состояние отправки анонсов: последний успешно отправленный snapshot, timestamps попыток/успехов full sync и delta send, флаг `needsFullResync`, отслеживание disconnect для eviction. Все мутабельные поля доступны только через потокобезопасные методы (`View()`, `RecordFullSyncAttempt()`, `RecordFullSyncSuccess()`, `RecordDeltaSendSuccess()`). Владелец — `AnnounceStateRegistry`.

`AnnounceStateRegistry` — реестр per-peer `AnnouncePeerState`. Потокобезопасный для одновременного доступа из цикла анонсов и колбэков жизненного цикла сессий. Предоставляет `GetOrCreate`, `MarkDisconnected`, `MarkReconnected`, `EvictStale`, `MarkInvalid` и `Cleanup`. Disconnected-состояние удаляется через `2 * flapWindow`. Источник времени внедряется для тестов.

### Модель хранения

Внутреннее хранилище живёт в `routing.routeStore` (`internal/core/routing/route_store.go`) и хранит **per-`(Identity, Uplink)` `UplinkClaim`**, где `Uplink` — identity того direct peer'а, который анонсировал нам claim:

```go
type UplinkClaim struct {
    Uplink            PeerIdentity              // direct peer who told us this claim
    Hops              uint8                     // their announced hops + 1
    SeqNo             uint64                    // upstream wire SeqNo
    Source            RouteSource               // direct / hop_ack / announcement
    UpdatedAt         time.Time
    ExpiresAt         time.Time                 // zero for direct
    Withdrawn         bool
    Extra             json.RawMessage           // forward-compat wire metadata
    LastIngressOrigin PeerIdentity              // sticky wire-frame Origin (mixed-version)
    SeenOriginSeqs    map[PeerIdentity]uint64   // per-Origin high-water (lazy)
    AttestedSig       []byte                    // reserved для Phase 4 (mesh_attested_links_v1)
}
```

`LastIngressOrigin` и `SeenOriginSeqs` поддерживают mixed-version interop admission rules — см. "Mixed-version interop" под Ключевыми инвариантами ниже для full contract. Storage держит per-Identity bucket с до `MaxNextHopsPerOrigin` LIVE claims (имя knob сохранено ради operator stability; semantic post-A1 — K live UplinkClaims per Identity). Withdrawn claims (tombstones) живут вне K-counted slots и bypass cap entirely — SeqNo-resurrection guard не evict'ится под cap pressure.

Boundary `RouteEntry` синтезируется on demand через `toRouteEntry` (в `uplink_claim.go`): берёт хранимый `UplinkClaim` плюс destination `Identity` плюс table's `localOrigin` и производит wire-shaped значение с `Origin = localOrigin` (или fallback на `Identity` если `localOrigin` пустой). Этот синтез позволяет public Table API оставаться source-compatible с pre-Phase-1 callers, пока storage internals мигрировали.

### Ключевые инварианты

**Per-Identity SeqNo monotonicity.** Sequence numbers managed на двух уровнях:

- *Own-origin advance counter*: `seqCounters[Identity]` — монотонный счётчик для маршрутов, которые эта нода originates (direct peers). Он автоматически advance'ит в `AddDirectPeer` / `RemoveDirectPeer` / `InvalidateAllVia` и синхронизируется вперёд через `UpdateRoute` ТОЛЬКО когда accepted entry имеет `Source == RouteSourceDirect` И `Origin == localOrigin` (см. "Согласованность счётчика SeqNo" ниже — Source gate предотвращает poisoning счётчика из синтезированного `Origin == localOrigin` на hop_ack-promotion paths foreign SeqNo значениями).
- *Per-`(Identity, sender)` wire timeline*: каждый outbound wire emit (live winner, own-direct tombstone passthrough, broadcast withdrawal) получает свой SeqNo через `routeStore.nextOutboundSeqLockedPerPeer` / `nextOutboundSeqLockedBroadcast`. Helpers поддерживают per-`(Identity, content-sig)` кэш плюс три watermark'а (`outboundMax`, `outboundBroadcastMax[Identity]`, `outboundPeerMax[(Identity, peer)]`), поэтому receiver наблюдает strictly монотонный SeqNo на каждой паре `(Identity, sender)` независимо от того, какой `claim.SeqNo` upstream'а контрибутил content. Watermark'и закрывают два A→B→A flavour'а — broadcast-driven (own-direct fanout пересекающий per-peer cache) и per-peer winner-switch (alternate-uplink preference shift, advancing single peer past cached value). Оба запинены `TestAnnounceTo_*` regression suite'ами в `announce_builder_test.go`.

**Ключ дедупликации.** Пара `(Identity, Uplink)` уникально идентифицирует хранимый `UplinkClaim`. Разные uplink'и для одной destination Identity создают независимые claim'ы (multipath). Legacy boundary RouteEntry shape несёт поле `Origin`, но post-Phase-1 оно НЕ входит в dedup key — только `(Identity, NextHop=Uplink)` консультируется через `routeStore.findByUplinkLocked`.

**Live-vs-tombstone exclusivity на проводе.** При наличии live winner для Identity, own-direct tombstones для этой Identity SUPPRESS'ятся на проводе в `AnnounceProjectionFor` (storage retain'ит tombstone для локального SeqNo-resurrection guard'а). Emit'ив оба, `nextOutboundSeqLockedPerPeer` назначил бы tombstone'у строго больший SeqNo чем live winner'у (peerMax advance'ится на live emit), и receiver-side монотонный SeqNo timeline сошёлся бы на tombstone'е — drop'нув Identity, хотя мы только что предложили backup uplink. Tombstones ДА эмитятся когда live альтернативы нет.

**Mixed-version interop admission rules.** Pre-A1 transits используют per-Origin SeqNo counters и shift'ят свой per-Identity winner между Origin lineages per cycle. Post-A1 storage применяет пять admission rules в фиксированном порядке внутри `ApplyUpdate`, чтобы держать legacy stream interop intact:

1. Pre-check guard отклоняет cross-Origin updates, чей incoming Origin имеет recorded `SeenOriginSeqs` high-water at-or-above `entry.SeqNo` (stale-replay на own timeline этого Origin'а).
2. HopAck override preserve'ит хранимый `LastIngressOrigin` / `SeenOriginSeqs` когда entry пришла из `confirmRouteViaHopAck` (synthetic `Origin == localOrigin` из `Lookup`, не wire observation).
3. Cross-Origin live-vs-tombstone at equal SeqNo promote'ит live entry через тот же cap-aware `AdmitNew` detach+readmit, что используется в SeqNo > old branch'е.
4. Standard SeqNo branches (>, ==, <) — stale-SeqNo branch дополнительно admit'ит cross-Origin update когда он strictly improves on hops, trust, или replace'ит tombstone (cross-Origin lineage shift).
5. Reconfirmation TTL refresh gate — hops-only (`incoming.Hops == old.Hops`), НЕ source-equality — поэтому wire re-announce после HopAck promotion всё равно refresh'ит TTL.

Все пять правил dormant для A1-to-A1 traffic (post-A1 senders emit `Origin = localOrigin` constant across cycles, поэтому cross-Origin gates никогда не fire'ят).

**Split horizon.** При формировании анонса для peer A claims с `Uplink == A` пропускаются. Фиктивный `hops=16` withdrawal не отправляется — это нарушило бы receiver-side инвариант монотонности SeqNo.

**Семантика withdrawal.** Отзыв маршрута устанавливает `Hops = 16` (бесконечность) и требует строго `SeqNo > old.SeqNo`. На проводе только origin может отправить withdrawal. При отключении peer'а `RemoveDirectPeer` отзывает own-origin direct-маршруты (возвращаются как wire-ready `[]AnnounceEntry` с уже инкрементированным SeqNo) и молча инвалидирует transit-маршруты локально. Транзитные ноды не генерируют wire-withdrawal для чужих маршрутов.

**Иерархия доверия.** Для каждой тройки: `direct > hop_ack > announcement`. При одинаковом SeqNo источник с более высоким доверием заменяет менее доверенный. Подтверждение одной тройки через hop_ack не влияет на другие тройки, даже при общем NextHop.

**Порядок выбора маршрута.** `Lookup()` ранжирует маршруты через Phase 2 `CompositeScore` (базовый hop-count term + source-trust бонус + RTT бонус + health penalty — формула в секции «Здоровье маршрутов и composite scoring» ниже и в `docs/protocol/route_health.md`). Source trust по-прежнему влияет через бонус (local/direct +20, hop_ack +10, announcement 0), поэтому при равных hops/health/RTT источник с большим доверием выигрывает; но в отличие от pre-Phase-2 sort'а, source trust больше не доминирует над hop count безусловно — Good 1-хоповый announcement может обогнать Bad 3-хоповый direct. `HealthDead` claims фильтруются до ранжирования с одним исключением: `RouteSourceDirect` (own-origin) claims остаются selectable даже при Dead и оцениваются с `Bad`-equivalent penalty, потому что lifecycle direct'ов session-driven, а не health-driven.

**Истечение TTL.** Learned-маршруты (из анонсов и hop_ack) имеют `ExpiresAt` (по умолчанию 120с с момента вставки). `TickTTL()` удаляет истёкшие записи и возвращает слайс identity, у которых истечение обнажило выживший не-withdrawn backup route — `routingTableTTLLoop` использует это для запуска `drainPendingForIdentities` и немедленной доставки через backup. Learned-маршруты обновляются естественным образом при переанонсировании соседом. Когда переанонс с тем же SeqNo приходит для expired записи, `UpdateRoute` принимает его как валидное обновление — origin не менял маршрут, а просто переподтверждает его. Когда переанонс с теми же SeqNo, source и hops приходит для *живой* learned-записи — точное переподтверждение — `UpdateRoute` возвращает `RouteUnchanged` и продлевает `ExpiresAt` до `now + defaultTTL`. Wire-level переподтверждение продлевает время жизни, даже если ни одно поле, важное для delta-consumer, не изменилось. Без этого продления no-op suppression на стороне отправителя дала бы learned-маршрутам истечь между forced full sync (см. «Инвариант интервала refresh» ниже).
